<div id="page-1153236">
<h3><a name="page-1153236">CB05_0002</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>2</p>
<p>List No 1</p>
<p>Jan'y 3 [187]6</p>
<p>Mr. A. A. Barker</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>I hand you herewith<span class='line-break'> </span>List of unpaid Lots so that you may <span class='line-break'> </span>not take orders for interments therein <span class='line-break'> </span>without proof of payment</p>
<p>1836 Ornamental Ground - Simons<span class='line-break'> </span>4090 Lot. Dyer<span class='line-break'> </span>4116 "Hanson"<span class='line-break'> </span>4150  "Church"<span class='line-break'> </span>4171  "Sibley"<span class='line-break'> </span>4205  "Hovey"<span class='line-break'> </span>4391  "Skillings"<span class='line-break'> </span>4392  "Whitney"<span class='line-break'> </span><del>4397  "Bradlee"</del> Paid Jan 26<span class='line-break'> </span>4403  "Hobart"</p>
<p>I will notify you from time to time as these are <span class='line-break'> </span>paid.  All other numbers to 4427 included are paid for <span class='line-break'> </span>with the exceptions marked on List No 2.</p>
<p>J.W. Lovering Supt<span class='line-break'> </span>per Child</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1153237">
<h3><a name="page-1153237">CB05_0003</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>3</p>
<p>List No. 2</p>
<p>Jan'y 3 [187]6</p>
<p>Mr. A. A. Barker<span class='line-break'> </span>Dear Sir</p>

<div id="page-1153240">
<h3><a name="page-1153240">CB05_0006</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>6</p>
<p>Jany 10 [187]6</p>
<p>H. E. Sheldon Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Your favor of Jan'y 7<sup>th</sup> just rec'd.<span class='line-break'> </span>I enclose a plan, showing dimensions of lot and distance <span class='line-break'> </span>from path, also the levels of lot &amp; path.<span class='line-break'> </span>The size of thelot is 14'x15', and you can place a curb<span class='line-break'> </span>not exceeding 1 foot in thickness outside of these dimensions,<span class='line-break'> </span>if it is less than 1 foot in thickness it must be placed its thickness<span class='line-break'> </span>outside of these dimensions.</p>
<p>The distance from inside of lot curb to outside of any curb<span class='line-break'> </span>or plots in path is 5'-6".<span class='line-break'> </span>The path is 3'6" below grade of <u>rear</u> of lot, and 2 ft below<span class='line-break'> </span>front of lot.</p>
<p>After the lot is curbed the grade of land outside the curb<span class='line-break'> </span>will remain as now, the lot itself being raised according <span class='line-break'> </span>to height of your curb.</p>
<p>When you pattern is selected, should be glad to <span class='line-break'> </span>arrange to set it for you, &amp; will give you good work at<span class='line-break'> </span>a reasonable price</p>
<p>Yours truly  J. W. Lovering, Supt.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1153241">
<h3><a name="page-1153241">CB05_0007</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>7</p>
<p>Jan'y 10  [187]6</p>
<p>Tho<sup>s</sup> Niles Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>The cost of building <span class='line-break'> </span>the foundation for the Mont 6' - 5in x 5' - 2 in<span class='line-break'> </span>10 ft deep as necessary in lot 3819<span class='line-break'> </span>will be from $60.<sup>00</sup> to $65.<sup>00</sup></p>
<p>The lot is 20 ft wide and deducting <span class='line-break'> </span>the width of Mont, there will be left<span class='line-break'> </span>6 ft 1/2 in on each side of foundation <span class='line-break'> </span>or 2 ft 3in for each interment which <span class='line-break'> </span>will probably be sufficient, if no <span class='line-break'> </span>room be wasted.</p>
<p>This is rather closer figuring<span class='line-break'> </span>than is absolutely safe and of <span class='line-break'> </span>course would not allow of brick <span class='line-break'> </span>catacombs being built</p>
<p>Very Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>Jas.W. Lovering Sup<sup>t</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1153242">

<p>Dear Sir -</p>
<p>Will you <span class='line-break'> </span>please give us the names of the <span class='line-break'> </span>interments in your lot. No 1829-.<span class='line-break'> </span>also their <del>names</del> ages -<span class='line-break'></span>-&amp; oblige</p>
<p>James W. Lovering Sup<sup>t</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>per B<span class='line-break'></span></p>

<div id="page-1153243">
<h3><a name="page-1153243">CB05_0009</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>9</p>
<p>Jan'y 10  [187]6</p>
<p>Elisha Bassett Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Your favor of yesterday is <span class='line-break'> </span>received</p>
<p>The trees whose shade was hurtfull to the <span class='line-break'> </span>grass in your lot #2874 have been removed with <span class='line-break'> </span>such others, in the vicinity, as was deemed proper</p>
<p>I see no reason, if proper care be excerised<span class='line-break'> </span>why the appearance of the lot should not <span class='line-break'> </span>improve in the future</p>
<p>Very Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>Jas W. Lovering Sup<sup>t</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1153244">
<h3><a name="page-1153244">CB05_0010</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>10</p>
<p>Jan'y 17  [187]6</p>
<p>Chas. D. Bagnall Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>The fence <span class='line-break'> </span>about lot #504 was removed<span class='line-break'> </span>immediately after the time the <span class='line-break'> </span>order was given.</p>
<p>The old iron brought in excess <span class='line-break'> </span>of the cost of removing $3.98<span class='line-break'> </span>which I will apply to the care <span class='line-break'> </span>of the lot, as far as it will go,<span class='line-break'> </span>this next summer or make <span class='line-break'> </span>such other disposition of it <span class='line-break'> </span>as may be proper -</p>
<p>Very Respectfully <span class='line-break'> </span>JW Lovering Sup<sup>t</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>per Child</p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-1153245">
<h3><a name="page-1153245">CB05_0011</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>11</p>
<p>Jan'y 19 [187]6</p>
<p>K.W Sherburne</p>
<p>Gentlemen</p>
<p>Please give me list<span class='line-break'> </span>price, and discount on 7x9 double thick <span class='line-break'> </span>German Glass, each 2<sup>d</sup> and  3<sup>d</sup> quality.</p>
<p>3<sup>d</sup> quote will do if it be free from <span class='line-break'> </span>bubbles</p>
<p>Respectfully <span class='line-break'> </span>J. W. Lovering Sup.<sup>t</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>per Child</p>

<div id="page-1153246">
<h3><a name="page-1153246">CB05_0012</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>12</p>
<p>Jany 22 [187]6</p>
<p>Mrs. Ann M. Buffum<span class='line-break'> </span>(Last door rear of 24 Myrtle St. B.)</p>
<p>Dear Madam</p>
<p>Your values<span class='line-break'> </span>favor of Jan 19 was received this<span class='line-break'> </span>morning. There is at this date<span class='line-break'> </span>a grave numbered 218 St. Matthews<span class='line-break'> </span>Lot which is for sale.</p>
<p>Price $25.<sup>00</sup> for grave $5.<sup>00</sup> for<span class='line-break'> </span>Interment &amp; Record both payable<span class='line-break'> </span>before the interment can be made<span class='line-break'> </span>Do not understand that I give you<span class='line-break'> </span>any refusal of the grave beyond<span class='line-break'> </span>Monday Morning.</p>
<p>Very Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>JW Lovering Sup<sup>t</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs</p>
<p>Jany 22 [187]6</p>
<p>George Rogers Esq<span class='line-break'> </span>Douglas Ave 60<span class='line-break'> </span>(Lot 547)</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>We will "Grade &amp; Sod<span class='line-break'> </span>Lot," "Paint Fence," and prepare and<span class='line-break'> </span>plant four (4) myrtle Graves for <span class='line-break'> </span>$64.50, if the work is all done<span class='line-break'> </span>at the same time, as, it can be<span class='line-break'> </span>done, at less cost then than if<span class='line-break'> </span>done separately.</p>
<p>The gate needs some repairs<span class='line-break'> </span>which are <u>not</u> included herein.</p>
<p>We would be pleased to receive<span class='line-break'> </span>your order for the work.</p>
<p>Very Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering Sup<sup>t</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1153247">
<h3><a name="page-1153247">CB05_0013</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>13</p>
<p>January 24 [187]6</p>
<p>Rob<sup>t</sup> Ross &amp; Sons</p>
<p>Gentlemen</p>
<p>I shall want (35) thirty five<span class='line-break'> </span>cords of hot manure suitable for hot [feds?] after [Feb 15?]<span class='line-break'> </span>At what price will you deliver it [illegible]<span class='line-break'> </span>may want it.</p>
<p>What price will you deliver through the summer<span class='line-break'> </span>165 cords, as fast as I may want it.</p>
<p>What price per cord will you charge to haul<span class='line-break'> </span>from Boston from about E Brookline &amp; Northampton<span class='line-break'> </span>Sts or that vicinity.</p>
<p>Yours &amp;c<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering Sup<sup>t</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs</p>
</div>

<div id="page-1153248">
<h3><a name="page-1153248">CB05_0014</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>14</p>
<p>January 24 [187]6</p>
<p>G.W. Moseley Esq<span class='line-break'> </span>80 E Brookline St. B.</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>I shall want thirty five (35) cords<span class='line-break'> </span>of hot manure for hot beds delivered as <u>I</u>may<span class='line-break'> </span>want to use it any time after Feb 15<span class='line-break'> </span>I shall also want about (165) one hundred sixty five cords<span class='line-break'> </span>delivered through the summer as <del>my convenience</del>^<sup>fast as we want to use it</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>I want your price for the 1<sup>st</sup> lot of 35 cords delivered<span class='line-break'> </span>here and also price of same at your stables.<span class='line-break'> </span>Also I want price for 165 cords both delivered here<span class='line-break'> </span>and at stable</p>
<p>I want the lowest possible prices for best quality<span class='line-break'> </span>of manure</p>
<p>Yours &amp;c<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W.Lovering Sup<sup>t</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs</p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-1153249">
<h3><a name="page-1153249">CB05_0015</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>15</p>
<p>January 24 [187]6</p>
<p>Mr. Jacob H. Hathorne<span class='line-break'> </span>10 Worcester Sq B.</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>I shall want (35) thirty five cords<span class='line-break'> </span>of hot manure suitable for hotbeds, after Feb 15.<span class='line-break'> </span>What price will you deliver it to me here for<span class='line-break'> </span>^<sup>and may want it</sup> and what price will you deliver at your stables<span class='line-break'> </span>I shall also want about (165) one hundred sixty five cords<span class='line-break'> </span>delivered through the summer at <u>my</u> convenience,<span class='line-break'> </span>at what price can you supply me with above<span class='line-break'> </span>lots, the manure to be of best quality --</p>
<p>Yours &amp;c<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering Sup<sup>t</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs<span class='line-break'> </span></p>

<div id="page-1153250">
<h3><a name="page-1153250">CB05_0016</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>16</p>
<p>Jany 24 [187]6</p>
<p>Joseph Collins Esq<span class='line-break'> </span>Gradener.</p>
<p>Dear Sir,</p>
<p>Oh and after Feb'y 1<sup>st</sup>, I shall expect<span class='line-break'> </span>you to keep rhe time of all men employed in your department.<span class='line-break'> </span>M<sup>c</sup>Donald &amp; Curtin will divide the Sunday work, once when<span class='line-break'> </span>extra men are needed the other men at greenhouses will divide<span class='line-break'> </span>it, also without any extra pay for Sundays, when the need stay only<span class='line-break'> </span>so long as may be necessary to take proper care of the plants.</p>
<p>None of the men on your book, will hereafter attend the gate<span class='line-break'> </span>or interments on Sundays, as I shall make other provision for that,<span class='line-break'> </span>and when the force is increased in the spring, you will allow<span class='line-break'> </span>no man except tho his greenhouse men M<sup>c</sup>Donald &amp; Curtin, and the<span class='line-break'> </span>gardener's teamster N. Collins, for any days when it is too wet to work<span class='line-break'> </span>except by special arrangement with me. I expect you to dismiss<span class='line-break'> </span>your men working in the grounds, whenever it is too wet to work<span class='line-break'> </span>for the advantage of the corporation, without regard to whether the <span class='line-break'> </span>other formen's men are working or not.</p>
<p>The weekly reports at the end of the month should show the same<span class='line-break'> </span>total number of days, which your time book shows, and you will<span class='line-break'> </span>be charged with as many days as are on your time book.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1153251">
<h3><a name="page-1153251">CB05_0017</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>17</p>
<p>unless you note on the foot of your weekly report the<span class='line-break'> </span>name of any man who has been away from you for<span class='line-break'> </span>a short time to assist either Mr. Barker or the foreman.</p>
<p>As a rule I do not care to have the man for the funerals<span class='line-break'> </span>taken from your department, and the section foreman should<span class='line-break'> </span>never be taken.</p>
<p>When the Spring opens a teamsters [will?] be appointed<span class='line-break'> </span>whom you can call on in case of need, the others I <span class='line-break'> </span>do not want taken from their work without orders from<span class='line-break'> </span>the foreman. If you have any doubt as to any of their arrangement<span class='line-break'> </span>please see me.</p>
<p>Yrs truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J. W. Lovering</p>
<p>Please see that the Sunday arrangement is understood as<span class='line-break'> </span>that all may be satisfied when payday comes.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1153252">
<h3><a name="page-1153252">CB05_0018</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>18</p>
<p>Jany 25<sup>th</sup> [187]6</p>
<p>J.M. Spelman Esq<span class='line-break'> </span>Chair. Comm on Mounds</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Enclosed is a plan which I offer as<span class='line-break'> </span>a substitute for the present plan for laying out that part<span class='line-break'> </span>of the Stone Farm between Magnolia, Swan &amp; Eagle Avenues and<span class='line-break'> </span>the Iron Fence.</p>
<p>A copy of the present laying out is in your posession or at<span class='line-break'> </span>the Boston office, and the proposed charges are shown on the<span class='line-break'> </span>enclosed plan in red.</p>
<p>I consider the advantage of the proposed plan to be that<span class='line-break'> </span>the laying out conforms more nearly with the natural<span class='line-break'> </span>surface, that the means of drainage will be better, and<span class='line-break'> </span>the curve &amp; winding avenues will present a more pleasing<span class='line-break'> </span>appearance than long and straight ones.</p>
<p>As work is now underway which would be somewhat effected by<span class='line-break'> </span>this change. I should be glad to know the decision of the<span class='line-break'> </span>committee as soon as convenient.</p>
<p>Resfectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J. W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />

<h3><a name="page-1153254">CB05_0020</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>20</p>
<p>Jany 26 [187]6</p>
<p>Clerk of the Selectmen of Watertown</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Please cause A. A. Barker<span class='line-break'> </span>Joseph Collins  Edw.<sup>d</sup> Patchett  Geo. E. S. Hutchins<span class='line-break'> </span>and E. F. Young to be apointed "special<span class='line-break'> </span>Policemen" all being employees of this<span class='line-break'> </span>Corporation</p>
<p>Very Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J. W. Lovering Sup.<sup>t</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs</p>
</div>

<div id="page-1153255">
<h3><a name="page-1153255">CB05_0021</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>21</p>
<p>Jany 26 [187]6</p>
<p>J. A. Jacobs Esq<span class='line-break'> </span>City Clerk</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Please cause A. A. Barker<span class='line-break'> </span>Joseph Collins  Edw.<sup>d</sup> Patchett and E. F. Young<span class='line-break'> </span>employees of this Corp<sup>n</sup> to be appointed Special<span class='line-break'> </span>Policemen and E. F. Young , Treasurer.</p>
<p>G. T. Barring having left our employ you<span class='line-break'> </span>will please <u>not</u> reappoint him special policeman<span class='line-break'> </span>on our account.</p>
<p>Very Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>Jas. W. Lovering Sup.<sup>t</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs</p>

<h3><a name="page-1153259">CB05_0025</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>25</p>
<p>Jan'y 27<sup>th</sup> [187]6</p>
<p>Mrs John Sargent</p>
<p>Dear Madam</p>
<p>I received a request in regard to <span class='line-break'> </span>changing the grave of lot #2131, on Asclepius path<span class='line-break'> </span>where I learn you are intending to put in steps<span class='line-break'> </span>&amp; [posts?] in the spring.</p>
<p>I am satisfied that the Trustees would not consent<span class='line-break'> </span>to any change of grade unless the lot was <u>curbed</u><span class='line-break'> </span>as well as posted. The grade of the lot now is 12<span class='line-break'> </span>inches above the path, and the stakes should be<span class='line-break'> </span>cut for this rise. I send you a sketch of the lot that<span class='line-break'> </span>your stone cutter may make the ^<sup>stakes of</sup> proper length to reach<span class='line-break'> </span>from lot to the path line.</p>
<p>When the front steps are ready, I should be very<span class='line-break'> </span>glad to have them set for you by our masons who<span class='line-break'> </span>do most all the work of this kind in the cemetery &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>who will give you entire satisfaction at a reasonable<span class='line-break'> </span>price. If you could secure a plan, I could give you<span class='line-break'> </span>the price beforehand. The corporation desires to do all work<span class='line-break'> </span>done in the cemetery as far as it may be acceptable to proprietors.</p>
<p>Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering Supt.</p>
</div>

<p>I have notified him to allow S. W. Hutchings 1/2 a<span class='line-break'> </span>day for every Sunday morning he is at gate, and<span class='line-break'> </span>that G. E. S. Hutchings and Mulvy Wailes be your<span class='line-break'> </span>regular men &amp; would be allowed all their time<span class='line-break'> </span>when present (cost per day) also that they would take their<span class='line-break'> </span>turn at being present on Sunday &amp; could be [alieved?]<span class='line-break'> </span>for it.</p>
<p>In case you need a second man on Sundays I expect<span class='line-break'> </span>you to keep one, only I should prefer as Hutchings &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>Mulvey are among the highest paid, not to pick out<span class='line-break'> </span>the most expensive men if possible.<span class='line-break'> </span>This will give you two men on every wet day &amp; one man on<span class='line-break'> </span>Sundays. <p>Yrs truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J. W. Lovering</p>

<div id="page-1153265">
<h3><a name="page-1153265">To Charles Cushman from Lovering (page 31)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>31</p>
<p>Feby 2<sup>nd</sup> [187]6</p>
<p>Charles Cushman Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>I have sent your gates to W<sup>m</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>Blake &amp; Co. on Charles St corner of Allen St Boston, who I<span class='line-break'> </span>think will be most successful in repairing your gates, as<span class='line-break'> </span>they are accustomed to that class of work.</p>
<p>After looking them over, M<sup>r</sup> Blake found that it would<span class='line-break'> </span>be almost impossible to restore them completely, and sent for<span class='line-break'> </span>me to come &amp; see them. I went with two of our Trustees and<span class='line-break'> </span>after talking with M<sup>r</sup> Blake, they decided that I have<span class='line-break'> </span>best inform you of the fact, and request you to see<span class='line-break'> </span>Mr Blake &amp; make such arrangements as you saw fit.</p>
<p>These trustees propose to offer a reward of $100<sup>00</sup> for the<span class='line-break'> </span>arrest &amp; conviction of the parties concerned in the removal<span class='line-break'> </span>&amp; injury of the gates, which out to be a sufficient induce<span class='line-break'></span>ment I should think to any parties in possession of any<span class='line-break'> </span>information to come forward, &amp; I sincerely hope that we<span class='line-break'> </span>may succeed in punishing the guilty parties.</p>
<p>Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering Supt.</p>
</div>
</div>

<p>In this caseyou can make it air tight<span class='line-break'> </span>with brick or slate and cement but in such<span class='line-break'> </span>manner that a second interment can be<span class='line-break'> </span>^<sup>made</sup>without damage to the tomb by removing the<span class='line-break'> </span>sealing.</p>

<div id="page-1153274">
<h3><a name="page-1153274">CB05_0037</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>37</p>
<p>Feby 15<sup>th</sup> [187]6</p>
<p>Andrew Robeson Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>The price for the perpetual care of your<span class='line-break'> </span>lot could be about $450 or 500. which covers the yearly<span class='line-break'> </span>care of the lot &amp; the repair or renewal of the sod or monument<span class='line-break'> </span>when necessary. This sum is definitely fixed by our<span class='line-break'> </span>Trustees, and they agree in their contract to keep the<span class='line-break'> </span>lot in order whether the sum proves sufficient or not.</p>
<p>You can deposit with the corporation any sum you<span class='line-break'> </span>see fit (say no less than $150) to be held by them in<span class='line-break'> </span>trust and the income expended on the lot. In this case<span class='line-break'> </span>they do not guarantee that the sum shall be sufficient,<span class='line-break'> </span>they only agree to spend the income as judiciously as possible.</p>
<p>In case you wish to make either of these arrangements<span class='line-break'> </span>I shall be happy to hear from you.</p>
<p>The address of the parties who had the care of the lot<span class='line-break'> </span>last season is P.O'Brien &amp; Son, 88 Sparks St. Cambridge.</p>
<p>In case you desire to choose your plants ^<sup>out here</sup> you can do so<span class='line-break'> </span>at our greenhouses near the Entrance. Our gardener's name<span class='line-break'> </span>is Collins.</p>
<p>Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering</p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-1153276">
<h3><a name="page-1153276">CB05_0038</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>38</p>
<p>Feby 17 [187]6</p>
<p>George F. Parkman Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Within an short time an order<span class='line-break'> </span>has been received from you for the care of your lot<span class='line-break'> </span>#326 for the coming service year.</p>
<p>Another order has been given by Miss E.S. Parkman<span class='line-break'> </span>to M<sup>r</sup> O'Brien who takes care of some of the lots in<span class='line-break'> </span>the cemetery.</p>
<p>The corporation has taken the care of your lot for a<span class='line-break'> </span>number of years, and I know of no reason why<span class='line-break'> </span>the work has not been satisfactory, so that I hope you<span class='line-break'> </span>will continue the care of the lot with the corporation.</p>
<p>It is the desire of the Trustees that all work in the<span class='line-break'> </span>Cemetery should be done by the regular Employees<span class='line-break'> </span>of the corporation as far as it is acceptable to proprietors<span class='line-break'> </span>of both.</p>
<p>Unless I hear from you to the contrary I will take<span class='line-break'> </span>the care of your lot as usual, and if anything in regard<span class='line-break'> </span>to the work is not satisfactory, I will endeavor to have it<span class='line-break'> </span>changed.</p>
<p>Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering Supt.</p>
</div>
</div>

Curtin, J M<sup>c</sup>Donald, &amp; W<sup>m</sup> Collins (teamster) will be paid<span class='line-break'> </span>for all days except Sunday when present , wet or dry.<span class='line-break'> </span>None of the other men will be paid except for such days<span class='line-break'> </span>as are sufficiently dry to work both men &amp; horses, when they are present.<span class='line-break'> </span>I have directed M<sup>r</sup> M<sup>c</sup> Arthur when it is too stormy for the<span class='line-break'> </span>men to continue working to ring the bell &amp; have the men stop,<span class='line-break'> </span>and that when too stormy to work he will not take them on<span class='line-break'> </span>in the morning or at noon. &amp; I wish to prevent any mis<span class='line-break'></span>understanding or confusion yours should stop work whenever his do.<span class='line-break'> </span>Please return the time of any man taken by M<sup>r</sup> Barker in case of need on<span class='line-break'> </span>your weekly sheet, with his name.</p>

<div id="page-1153289">
<h3><a name="page-1153289">CB05_0051</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>51</p>
<p>March 27 [187]6</p>
<p>Joseph Collins Esq<span class='line-break'> </span>Gardener</p>
<p>I desire to call your attention to the follow<span class='line-break'></span>ing points which I wish you would see that all<span class='line-break'> </span>men under your charge observe.<span class='line-break'> </span>1. There is to be no smoking in the Cemetery.<span class='line-break'> </span>2. No man must enter or leave the Cemetery except by gates.<span class='line-break'> </span>3. You will allow no man to leave a substitute, when about,<span class='line-break'> </span>nor allow him for any time he is not actually here without my<span class='line-break'> </span>written consent.<span class='line-break'> </span>4. See that the men close and fasten the gate on all fence<span class='line-break'> </span>lots where they work and that they do not leave tools, clothes,<span class='line-break'> </span>or dinner pails about the ground, nor eat their dinners on the<span class='line-break'> </span>lots or ornamental grounds, especially about the gate.<span class='line-break'> </span>5. No tools, horse carts or other property of the corporation are<span class='line-break'> </span>to be loaned, or used except for corporation work, or taken<span class='line-break'> </span>from the grounds except for corporation work under any circum<span class='line-break'></span>stances. I consider you responsible for the  white horse &amp; cart<span class='line-break'> </span>^<sup>at all times</sup> for any other horse &amp; cart <u>while</u> in your employ.<span class='line-break'> </span>Have tools well put away every Saturday night.</p>
<p>Yours truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering Supt.</p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-1153290">
<h3><a name="page-1153290">CB05_0052</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>52</p>
<p>March 27 [187]6</p>
<p>C. M<sup>c</sup>Arthur Esq<span class='line-break'> </span>Foreman</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>I desire to call your attention to the following<span class='line-break'> </span>points which I wish you would see are observed by all<span class='line-break'> </span>men under your charge.<span class='line-break'> </span>1. There is to be no smoking in the Cemetery or Buildings.<span class='line-break'> </span>2. No man must leave or enter the Cemetery except by the gates.<span class='line-break'> </span>3. You will allow no man to leave a substitute, when about, nor<span class='line-break'> </span>allow him for any time not actually here, without my written consent.<span class='line-break'> </span>4. Men must close &amp; fasten the gates of all lots where they have<span class='line-break'> </span>been at work, and must not leave their tools, clothes, or dinner pails <span class='line-break'> </span>about the grounds, nor must they take their dinners on the lots or on the<span class='line-break'> </span>ornamental grounds, especially about the gate.<span class='line-break'> </span>5. No tools, carts, harnesses, horses, derricks are to be loaned under<span class='line-break'> </span>any circumstances nor to be taken from the grounds except<span class='line-break'> </span>for Cemetery work. You will consider I consider yourself as having charge<span class='line-break'> </span>of all derricks, carts &amp; horses except the white horse &amp; wagon.</p>
<p>Yours truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering Supt.</p>
</div>
</div>

<h3><a name="page-1153291">CB05_0054</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>54</p>
<p>March 27 [187]6</p>
<p>C. M<sup>c</sup>Arthur Esq foreman</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>On Saturday April 1<sup>st</sup> the spring pay <span class='line-break'> </span>will commence. I wish you would see that all whose<span class='line-break'> </span>names are on your book are notified that there will<span class='line-break'> </span>be a reduction from the prices paid in 1875, in April.<span class='line-break'> </span>Any man desiring to know at what rate he will be<span class='line-break'> </span>paid can inquire at the office of M<sup>r</sup> Childs with<span class='line-break'> </span>whom I will leave a list.</p>
<p>The teamsters pay will be $1.75 per day, all days to be<span class='line-break'> </span>counted except Sundays, wet or dry, when they are prsent.<span class='line-break'> </span>This is a much smaller reduction than is made for most<span class='line-break'> </span>of the men, but I take into consideration that they have to<span class='line-break'> </span>come early to take care of the horses and that they will be<span class='line-break'> </span>expected to get to work promptly at 7 o'clock and 10 o'clock &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>not leave until the bell rings. I expect they will be on hand<span class='line-break'> </span>early evenings to give the horses good care, &amp; stay long enough at<span class='line-break'> </span>night. Teamsters, Engineer, S. Elder so expressed concern from overseer.<span class='line-break'> </span>That Engineer, firemen ^<sup>P.W. Hutchins</sup>, Patchell, Day, Rainey, Eldan J. O'Hare, [?] will<span class='line-break'> </span>be a [?] for their time in lost wealth when present; the others will be [?]<span class='line-break'> </span>only for each day as present, when everything is such that they can look</p>
</div>

<p>March 21<sup>st</sup> [187]6</p>
<p>J.M. Spelman Prest.</p>
<p>Dear Sir,</p>
<p>I respectfully request I may be<span class='line-break'> </span>authorized to purchase a Safe for the protection of<span class='line-break'> </span>orders for work interments, and the records &amp; books most<span class='line-break'> </span>valuable here.</p>
<p>At present there is no sufficient protection against<span class='line-break'> </span>either fire or any ill &amp; displeased oerson.</p>
<p>During the summer months there are times here<span class='line-break'> </span>when there are orders for work amounting to fifteen<span class='line-break'> </span>or more thousand dollars in aggregate.</p>
<p>A safe 49 3/4 inches high, 36 inches wide and 19 inches deep<span class='line-break'> </span>made by E.R. Morse, and somewhat used by the Eliot<span class='line-break'> </span>Savings Bank, tho' still in good condition, can be purchase<span class='line-break'> </span>for $350 delivered, about one half the cost of a new one.</p>

<h3><a name="page-1153295">CB05_0058</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>58</p>
<p>March 20 [187]6</p>
<p>Mrs. Sarah Millett<span class='line-break'> </span>Rep. of Lot #2840</p>
<p>Dear Madam</p>
<p>I enclose postal<span class='line-break'> </span>card in blank for an order to<span class='line-break'> </span>care for this lot at an annual<span class='line-break'> </span>charge of $5.00; you will observe<span class='line-break'> </span>that by signing at the foot of<span class='line-break'> </span>the card that the order will be<span class='line-break'> </span>executed from year to year until<span class='line-break'> </span>forbid, This is simply to save<span class='line-break'> </span>you the trouble of giving, an, order<span class='line-break'> </span>each year. Of course you suit<span class='line-break'> </span>your own convenience in this matter.<span class='line-break'> </span>At that price we will keep the lot<span class='line-break'> </span>neat and orderly, the grass cut and<span class='line-break'> </span>the myrtle free of weeds &amp;c, But it<span class='line-break'> </span>does not include any repairs to<span class='line-break'> </span>myrtle which may in the future become<span class='line-break'> </span>necessary.</p>
<p>Very Resp'y<span class='line-break'> </span>Jas. W. Lovering Supt.<span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs</p>
<p>Mch 24 [187]6</p>
<p>Mr. Edw<sup>d</sup> Russell</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>What are<span class='line-break'> </span>your wishes regarding flowers<span class='line-break'> </span>in lot. 4377; similar to<span class='line-break'> </span>last year? ,or, are you as yet<span class='line-break'> </span>undecided. I remind you<span class='line-break'> </span>this early, that the matter may not be overlooked.</p>
<p>Very Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering Sup.<sup>t</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs</p>
</div>

<h3><a name="page-1153298">CB05_0061</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>61</p>
<p>March 4<sup>th</sup> [187]6</p>
<p>Thos Gray Esq</p>
<p>My dear Sir</p>
<p>Your favor of yesterday with card<span class='line-break'> </span>for 1876 at hand.</p>
<p>I am sorry to learn that the vase was not to <span class='line-break'> </span>your liking last summer, but I hope this year it may<span class='line-break'> </span>please you better &amp; be as it ought to be, as I have called to<span class='line-break'> </span>special attention of our gardeners to it.</p>
<p>Should you see, at any time, in the work done <span class='line-break'> </span>for you by the Corporation anything unsatisfactory, I<span class='line-break'> </span>should consider it a favor if you would call my<span class='line-break'> </span>attention to it, that any mistake or neglect might be<span class='line-break'> </span>rectified.</p>
<p>Yours very truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering</p>
</div>
</div>

<p>J.M. Spelman Esq<span class='line-break'> </span>Prest.</p>

<p>A platform scale is wanted at the <span class='line-break'> </span>Cemetery for the purpose of weighing lead, paints &amp; oils, cement<span class='line-break'> </span>grain &amp;c &amp;c, both for the purpose of making proper charges<span class='line-break'> </span>for amounts of material used in work on lots, and also<span class='line-break'> </span>for ascertaining that the corporation actually receives the amount<span class='line-break'> </span>of material paid for.</p>
<p>A platform scale which will weigh 5h 700 lbs can be<span class='line-break'> </span>purchased for ($24.00) twenty four dollars.</p>
<p>Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering</p>

<div class="page-content">
<p>64</p>
<p>March 27 [187]6</p>
<p>E.F. Young Esq<span class='line-break'> </span>Engineer</p>
<p>On and after April 1<sup>st</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>your pay will be at the rate of<span class='line-break'> </span>$2.30) two dollars and thirty cents<span class='line-break'> </span>per day for each day present except<span class='line-break'> </span>Sunday. On Sunday you will be<span class='line-break'> </span>expected to take your turn with the<span class='line-break'> </span>fireman in letting on the Fountains<span class='line-break'> </span>without extra pay.</p>
<p>I have notified Mr. M<sup>c</sup>Arthur that he<span class='line-break'> </span>is to allow in persons for time when<span class='line-break'> </span>about, even if a substitute is about<span class='line-break'> </span>without my written consent for<span class='line-break'> </span>each case.</p>
<p>Yours truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt.</p>
<p>March 27 [187]6</p>
<p>Joseph Collins Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>You may allow<span class='line-break'> </span>P. Curtin, J M<sup>c</sup>Donald their holidays &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>they can take their time in being present.<span class='line-break'> </span>Also allow W. Collins as teamster his<span class='line-break'> </span>holidays.</p>
<p>If the men are needed on Fast day<span class='line-break'> </span>at [?] keep them &amp; allow them<span class='line-break'> </span>for it. On the other holidays they will not<span class='line-break'> </span>be needed.</p>
<p>Yours truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering Supt.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>

<h3><a name="page-1153304">CB05_0067</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>67</p>
<p>March 29 [187]6</p>
<p>Mrs. E.P. Shattuck, [?] Eliza Sutton, Peabody, Mass.</p>
<p>Dear Madam</p>
<p>Lot #1533 Chestnut A. is<span class='line-break'> </span>worth about $400 to $450.</p>
<p>In regard to your inquiries about #1340 Cypress A.<span class='line-break'> </span>The Trustees will probably make no objection<span class='line-break'> </span>to taking the lot under perpetual care as it<span class='line-break'> </span>now is, with the Fence, after the same is<span class='line-break'> </span>painted. They would prefer, probably to take the<span class='line-break'> </span>lot without any fence cast or anything of the<span class='line-break'> </span>kind, with simply a granite post at each corner<span class='line-break'> </span>to mark the boundaries, but do not insist, upon<span class='line-break'> </span>the removal of the fence. In fact the objections<span class='line-break'> </span>to a fence apply with equal force to curbs<span class='line-break'> </span>or other enclosures. The probable cost of Perpetual<span class='line-break'> </span>Care of this lot after the fence is painted will be<span class='line-break'> </span>$650 to $700. - We can paint the fence when you<span class='line-break'> </span>desire it done.</p>
<p>Very Respectfully</p>
<p>Jas W. Lovering Sup<sup>t</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs</p>
</div>
</div>

If the bill<span class='line-break'> </span>has been paid, I will furnish you the usual<span class='line-break'> </span>quantity of plants viz., $3.00 worth, this year without<span class='line-break'> </span>charge. <p>E.J. Andrews Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>The Headstones in #1290,<span class='line-break'> </span>five in number, should be dowelled at a<span class='line-break'> </span>cost of about $15.00.</p>
<p>The Gate could probably be repaired,<span class='line-break'> </span>after a fashion, but I should think that<span class='line-break'> </span>a new Gate would be more satisfactory.<span class='line-break'> </span>I cannot give you exact figures on the<span class='line-break'> </span>gate but should judge it might be repaired<span class='line-break'> </span>for, say $3.50 or a new one furnished for<span class='line-break'> </span>$8.00 to $10.00. <p>April 7 [187]6</p>
<p>Mr H.B. Runey</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>The bill for the<span class='line-break'> </span>Int. &amp; Rec. of Sarah S. Hannaford in lot 4279, in this<span class='line-break'> </span>Cemetery was with the addition of  ['Rune'?] furnished,<span class='line-break'> </span>in total $6.00  The bill was so made out and<span class='line-break'> </span>so receipted and was delivered to you by<span class='line-break'> </span>mistake on the part of the man who took $5.00<span class='line-break'> </span>in place of what the bill called for.<span class='line-break'> </span>I acknowledge hereby the receipt, of $5.00 on this<span class='line-break'> </span>account -</p>
<p>Please send me by return mail the receipt<span class='line-break'> </span>obtained today, and I will, abate the charge for<span class='line-break'> </span>['Rum'?] and sender you a corrected bill<span class='line-break'> </span>receipted for $5.00.</p>
<p>Please give this matter immediate attention.</p>
<p>Very  Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering Sup.<sup>t</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs.</p>

<p>73</p>
<p>April 8<sup>th</sup> [187]6</p>
<p>Edw<sup>d</sup> T. Doesser Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>As I learn that you were<span class='line-break'> </span>much disappointed on visiting the Cemetery lately,<span class='line-break'> </span>to find your lot unfinished, I desire to explain<span class='line-break'> </span>how this happened.</p>
<p>The stone for Mr Carter's lot was received November 19<sup>th</sup> &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>was set and the sodding finished Nov 27<sup>th</sup> and was<span class='line-break'> </span>one of the last, if not the very last lot sodded last fall<span class='line-break'> </span>as after December 1<sup>st</sup> the weather rarely allows us to<span class='line-break'> </span>carry on any work requiring sodding.</p>
<p>On the 30<sup>th</sup> day of November the stone for your lot was<span class='line-break'> </span>rec'd and it was set before Dec 11<sup>th</sup>.</p>
<p>I should have been exceedingly glad to have finished<span class='line-break'> </span>the tomb last fall, but the stone was received so late<span class='line-break'> </span>that it was impossible. It shall be finished early<span class='line-break'> </span>this spring.</p>
<p>This explanation will I trust be satisfactory.</p>
<p>Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering Supt.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />

<div id="page-1153313">
<h3><a name="page-1153313">CB05_0076</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>76</p>
<p>Apr 16<sup>th</sup> [187]6</p>
<p>Francis Thompson Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>The cost of releading &amp; resetting the <span class='line-break'> </span>curbing &amp; on lots 3518 and 3519 was $53 beside the<span class='line-break'> </span>foundations which were $57 more (One large &amp; 4 small ones)<span class='line-break'> </span>$110 in all.</p>
<p>This makes 1/2 cost of releading &amp; resetting &amp;c. $26.50 and<span class='line-break'> </span>the care^<sup>$4</sup>, plants &amp; top dressing^<sup>$3.50</sup> were $9.50 more on each lot,<span class='line-break'> </span>making the expense $36.00 per lot beside the foundations.</p>
<p>I have received no orders for care of your lots for this<span class='line-break'> </span>year. The price will be $1. per lot less than last<span class='line-break'> </span>year, that is for care, plants &amp; top dressing $8.50 per lot<span class='line-break'> </span>or $17.00 for both.</p>
<p>If you desire us to take care of the lots please<span class='line-break'> </span>sign the postal cards &amp; return.</p>
<p>Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt.</p>

<h3><a name="page-1153316">CB05_0079</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>79</p>
<p>April 11<sup>th</sup> [187]6</p>
<p>J.M. Spelman Esq<span class='line-break'> </span>Prest.</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>I send you a plan for the construction<span class='line-break'> </span>of 56 catacombs, sizes shown on plan, to take the place of<span class='line-break'> </span>the section now there.</p>
<p>The catacombs are to be built of hard brick and slate, with<span class='line-break'> </span>slate divisions in front and marble doors. The arch and end<span class='line-break'> </span>wall to be lined with face brick, and the arch to be<span class='line-break'> </span>well covered with asphalt. The floor to be tiled with slate<span class='line-break'> </span>and marble tiles laid on a suitable foundation. The cost of<span class='line-break'> </span>this would be $4350, which includes no grading about the tomb, but <span class='line-break'> </span>any necessary excavation for foundations to, and provides for new<span class='line-break'> </span>material entire.</p>
<p>There will be stock of sufficient value in the present section to <span class='line-break'> </span>pay for its renewal &amp; perhaps something more.</p>
<p>To take off the present granite tiles and relay them after asphalting the<span class='line-break'> </span><table class='tabular'><thead><span class='line-break'> </span><tr><th>arch, and relaying 2 courses of the brick work if necessary will cost</th> <th>$550.<span class='line-break'> </span></th></tr></thead> <tbody> <tr><td>To tile the vestibule, including a thorough foundation.</td> <td>460</td> </tr> <tr><td>[Total]</td> <td>$1010.</td> </tr> </tbody> </table> Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering</p>
</div>
</div>

<p>April 15 [187]6</p>
<p>Mason &amp; Buffum</p>
<p>Gentlemen,</p>
<p>When you were<span class='line-break'> </span>paid for putting a striker upon the Bell<span class='line-break'> </span>here, you stated , that, if everything was not<span class='line-break'> </span>satisfactory you would make it so on being<span class='line-break'> </span>notified.</p>
<p>The striker is not now, nor has, it ever<span class='line-break'> </span>been what we were justified in expecting for<span class='line-break'> </span>the money.</p>
<p>You have been notified by the facts in<span class='line-break'> </span>the case a number of time without result.</p>
<p>You will oblige me by giving this matter<span class='line-break'> </span>immediate attention without causing us<span class='line-break'> </span>further trouble.</p>
<p>Very Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>Jas. W. Lovering Sup.<sup>t</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs</p>

<div id="page-1153324">
<h3><a name="page-1153324">CB05_0087</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>87</p>
<p>April 18<sup>th</sup> [187]6</p>
<p>S.T. Snow Esq<span class='line-break'> </span>Chair. Comm. on Lots</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>In answer to your inquiry as<span class='line-break'> </span>to the cost of perpetual care of the sod on single lots<span class='line-break'> </span>in the old Cemetery, I hand you the following figures which<span class='line-break'> </span>are the actual amounts charged to 29 lots of different<span class='line-break'> </span>sizes from 1870 to 1875 inclusive, a period of six years. These<span class='line-break'> </span>figures include all moneys spent for the care, top dressing spending<span class='line-break'> </span>of the lots and repairs &amp; renewal of sod. During the three years<span class='line-break'> </span>(1873,4,5) which I have had the care of the lots, the cost<span class='line-break'> </span>has been charged for at the same rates as for work done<span class='line-break'> </span>for proprietors, and therefore there was some 10% profit on<span class='line-break'> </span>this work, as there are no bad debts to allow for during<span class='line-break'> </span>1870, 1 and 2, the work  done on perpetual care lots appears<span class='line-break'> </span>to be charged for at rates higher than these charged proprietors<span class='line-break'> </span>for the same work.</p>
<p>I consider therefore that the actual cost is a little less than<span class='line-break'> </span>the table shows, ($1.019 pr sq foot.)</p>
<p>(over)</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />

<h3><a name="page-1153326">CB05_0089</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>89</p>
<p>April 20 [187]6</p>
<p>J.E. Davis Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Your favor of yesterday<span class='line-break'> </span>is received. I have looked at lot 1052<span class='line-break'> </span>Chestnut Ave and find that there is hardly<span class='line-break'> </span>an inch of loam on the lot.</p>
<p>I can see no objection to raising the grade<span class='line-break'> </span>say 10 inches, there ought to be as much as<span class='line-break'> </span>10 inches of loam under the sod.</p>
<p>I will fill in 10 inches good loam and sod<span class='line-break'> </span>with good sod and leave in good order<span class='line-break'> </span>for $60.<sup>00</sup> and will give you the benefit<span class='line-break'> </span>of any reduction there may be in the cost of work.</p>
<p>The cost of a foundation expends on the size of<span class='line-break'> </span>the base stone and not on size of headstone.<span class='line-break'> </span>A foundation for a Stone when the base 2 ft long &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>1 ft wide would cost about $4.<sup>00</sup>; other sizes on<span class='line-break'> </span>the same scale. I enclose blank order for<span class='line-break'> </span>are &amp;c which please fill as suits you &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>return to</p>
<p>Very Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering Sup.<sup>t</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs</p>

<p>April 28<sup>th</sup> [187]6</p>
<p>J.M. Spelman Esq<span class='line-break'> </span>Prest.</p>
<p>I estimate the cost of building in the New Receiving<span class='line-break'> </span>Tomb, a section of fifty six (56) catacombs according to the plan<span class='line-break'> </span>I have [seen?], in place of then now there; at $4350, which includes<span class='line-break'> </span>all necessary excavations and the removal of the present sections, but<span class='line-break'> </span>no grading &amp; sodding.</p>
<p>The [walls?] are to be of hard brick on good foundation, all laid in<span class='line-break'> </span>cement; the catacombs to have slate shelves, brick division [?]<span class='line-break'> </span>faced with slate, and marble doors. The arch of large brick fitted with<span class='line-break'> </span>face brick, and coated with asphalt. The tiles may be of slate and marble<span class='line-break'> </span>or of light colors if desired.</p>
<p>The vestibule can be tiled &amp; cleaned for $460.00 and the granite<span class='line-break'> </span>arch taken off and relaid after repairing the arch &amp; coating it with<span class='line-break'> </span>asphalt, the front cleaned &amp; painted for $550. Total on vestibule $1010.--</p>
<p>I have asked Treas<sup>rs</sup> Cook &amp; Ryan to estimate on the cost of a<span class='line-break'> </span>simple iron door.</p>
<p>The total cost besides the door for the new section &amp; repairs to vestibule<span class='line-break'> </span>is therefore $5360 to which $250 or at any rate no more than<span class='line-break'> </span>$300 must be added for grading &amp; sodding over arch and above rear of tomb.</p>
<p>Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering </p>

<p>I have directed that the sod <span class='line-break'></span>about the mont. be repaired and<span class='line-break'> </span>that the graves be changed as per<span class='line-break'> </span>your verbal directions. I have<span class='line-break'> </span>added this to the order as I am<span class='line-break'> </span>under instructions from the Trustees<span class='line-break'> </span>to do no work for Proprietors, or others<span class='line-break'> </span>without written directions, in order to<span class='line-break'> </span>prevent misunderstanding.</p>
<p>Very Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering Sup.<sup>t</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs.</p>
</div>

<h3><a name="page-1153351">CB05_0114</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>114</p>
<p>May 12 [187]6</p>
<p>Messrs Parker &amp; Gannett</p>
<p>Dear Sirs</p>
<p>Your favor of the 11<sup>th</sup> just received<span class='line-break'> </span>The corporation keep the grass cut and make all<span class='line-break'> </span>necessary repairs to the bedding on all lots sold by them, without<span class='line-break'> </span>any additional days per annum, a portion of the price of the<span class='line-break'> </span>lot being laid aside for this purpose.</p>
<p>In some parts of the Cemetery lots are sold when the proprietors<span class='line-break'> </span>can fence or curb with stone, but cannot enclose with a hedge.<span class='line-break'> </span>Lots of 300 sq feet, the size usually laid out cost from $850 to $1150<span class='line-break'> </span>according to locations. These are in the Old part of the cemetery.<span class='line-break'> </span>On the Southern slope of the Tower is some desirable land for<span class='line-break'> </span>lots, quite high; here lots are lain out on the lawn plan, which<span class='line-break'> </span>restricts the proprietors from erecting any fence or stone curbing.</p>
<p>The lots are marked with stone posts level with the sod; monuments<span class='line-break'> </span>can be erected, also headstones not exceeding 2 1/2 feet in height.<span class='line-break'> </span>A 300 ft lot on path costs $660 which includes the lot, the perpetual<span class='line-break'> </span>care of the graves, and the boundary posts. The lots are now all complete<span class='line-break'> </span>except [for posts?]. On the avenue, the same size lot costs $810.</p>
<p>Should be happy to meet your Mr Parker at the cemetery &amp; show<span class='line-break'> </span>him the lots.</p>
<p>Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>

Last year the charges <span class='line-break'> </span>were <span class='line-break'> </span><table class='tabular'><thead><span class='line-break'> </span><tr><th>Care</th> <th>6.00<span class='line-break'> </span></th></tr></thead> <tbody> <tr><td>Plants</td> <td>3.00</td> </tr> <tr><td>Top Dressing</td> <td>5.00</td> </tr> <tr><td>Watering 2 Vases</td> <td>2.00</td> </tr> </tbody> </table> The Trustees having<span class='line-break'> </span>reduced the price of care<span class='line-break'> </span>&amp; Top dressing the charges<span class='line-break'> </span>for 1876 will be respectively<span class='line-break'> </span>Care 5.00 Pl 3.00 T.D. $3.75 &amp; Watering 2 Vases 2.00</p>
<p>Please advise me whether you will<span class='line-break'> </span>fill the vases yourself, or, do you<span class='line-break'> </span>wish us to fill them for you.</p>
<p>Very Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering Sup<sup>t</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs</p>

<h3><a name="page-1153362">CB05_0125</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>125</p>
<p>May 22 [187]6</p>
<p>Mrs. Flora A. Sawyer</p>
<p>Dear Madam</p>
<p>The order left here<span class='line-break'> </span>by you for the care of 2583 with the<span class='line-break'> </span>price named at $4.00 I must respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>decline to execute. The price for care<span class='line-break'> </span>being fixed by the Trustees, it does not<span class='line-break'> </span>come within my province to alter them.<span class='line-break'> </span>Last year by our regular scale you would<span class='line-break'> </span>have been charged $8.00^<sup>for care</sup> where as you were charged only<span class='line-break'> </span>$5.00 owing to error made at some previous<span class='line-break'> </span>time. This year (1876) owing to the reduction in price<span class='line-break'> </span>the regular charge should be $7.00 for care. All<span class='line-break'> </span>that I can do is simply to make no alteration<span class='line-break'> </span>in the price at all. I return the card marked<span class='line-break'> </span>for your attention, and also an order in<span class='line-break'> </span>blank not doubting but the above will satis<span class='line-break'></span>factorily explain the state of care.</p>
<p>Very Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering Sup.<sup>t</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs</p>
<p>May 20 [187]6</p>
<p>Mr. Geo. B. Wilbur</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>I enclose<span class='line-break'> </span>card, of blank order, for care<span class='line-break'> </span>of lot 3611.</p>
<p>The prices for care of lots <span class='line-break'> </span>of different sizes is fixed by<span class='line-break'> </span>the Trustees at $4.00 per year<span class='line-break'> </span>for a 300 ft lot, other lots being in<span class='line-break'> </span>proportion; which is a reduction<span class='line-break'> </span>of about 20% from prices heretofore<span class='line-break'> </span>charged. Heretofore you have been<span class='line-break'> </span>charged less than the regular<span class='line-break'> </span>rates which accounts for there<span class='line-break'> </span>being no change in the charge<span class='line-break'> </span>for 3611.</p>
<p>Very Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering Sup.<sup>t</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs</p>

<div class="page-content">
<p>May 24 [187]6</p>
<p>Mrs. A.C. Draper</p>
<p>Dear Madam</p>
<p>As yet no order has been received<span class='line-break'> </span>for the care of Lot #1658.  The lot has for several years<span class='line-break'> </span>past been taken care of by the Corp.<sup>n</sup> and the Monument<span class='line-break'> </span>cover removed in the spring, stored through the summer<span class='line-break'> </span>and put on before the winter began at an annual expense<span class='line-break'> </span>of five dollars for care and three for plants.</p>
<p>The cover has been removed this spring by, us &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>stored and although I know of no reason why the work done<span class='line-break'> </span>has been unsatisfactory, the lot has been given to other<span class='line-break'> </span>Gardeners, I learn, to take care of.  I hope you will<span class='line-break'> </span>reconsider this and still have the Corporation do the work<span class='line-break'> </span>as heretofore.  Should you prefer to have the lot, taken<span class='line-break'> </span>care of by, other parties, you will of course arrange with<span class='line-break'> </span>them to take charge of your monument cover, or I can<span class='line-break'> </span>do that part, if you prefer but shall in such can<span class='line-break'> </span>of course make a seperate charge for it.</p>

<div class="page-content">
<p>145</p>
<p>May 31 [187]6</p>
<p>Mr. Edward Austin</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Your favor of May 29 is<span class='line-break'> </span>received. The myrtle was replaced last fall<span class='line-break'> </span>as you directed but was killed by severe<span class='line-break'> </span>weather during the winter - all the new myrtle here<span class='line-break'> </span>with hardly an exception, during the winter.</p>
<p>The winds were so severe and there being so<span class='line-break'> </span>little snow that it was impossible to keep<span class='line-break'> </span>a sufficient covering on to protect the roots.</p>
<p>The myrtle in your lot was replaced this spring<span class='line-break'> </span>and as yet has hardly had time to make much<span class='line-break'> </span>growth. I trust this will be satisfactory. As to<span class='line-break'> </span>the holly bush I have to acknowledge an error.</p>
<p>The matter was overlooked in some way last fall<span class='line-break'> </span>and spring. I will see to it that it is put in<span class='line-break'> </span>the lot next spring if you wish it done.</p>
<p>Very Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering Sup.<sup>t</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs</p>

<p>As the Corporation has heretofor always done<span class='line-break'> </span>the work on the lot I presume some mistake<span class='line-break'> </span>has been made as to persons. We will<span class='line-break'> </span>do all the above work and take care of the<span class='line-break'> </span>lot for 1876 for $40.<sup>00</sup></p>
<p>I shall be very glad to receive an order and<span class='line-break'> </span>will have it executed immediately.</p>
<p>Very Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering Sup.<sup>t</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs</p>

<p>I find that the slate front for<span class='line-break'> </span>our Receiving Tomb has progressed as far now that<span class='line-break'> </span>it cannot be fitted to a templet, although all the<span class='line-break'> </span>uprights are cut by a guage.</p>
<p>I should be glad to have your estimate for<span class='line-break'> </span>furnishing the 128 catacomb tomb of italian<span class='line-break'> </span>marble best quality, highly polished &amp; wells finished<span class='line-break'> </span>in all aspects 7/8" thick; in each door four holes to<span class='line-break'> </span>be drilled for the two handles, and also two [dowels?] to<span class='line-break'> </span>be put in top of each door, leaded in, to fit the<span class='line-break'> </span>holes drilled in the slate; all necessary fitting to<span class='line-break'> </span>make a good piece of work included. Also a belt<span class='line-break'> </span>course plain, of Italian Marble, highly polished @ face<span class='line-break'> </span>&amp; bottom edge, to make 92'-8* in length, 6" high and<span class='line-break'> </span>5" thick, the whole delivered here.</p>

<div id="page-1153403">
<h3><a name="page-1153403">CB05_0165</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>165</p>
<p>June 12<sup>th</sup> [187]6</p>
<p>T.F. M<sup>c</sup>Gann Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>I have your sample of the han<span class='line-break'></span>dles of compositions you propose to make for me &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>should consider them satisfactory if fully up to<span class='line-break'> </span>sample &amp; should prefer them fully as heavy as the<span class='line-break'> </span>pattern. The sample is a little light.</p>
<p>You may make one 255 handles which with<span class='line-break'> </span>the sample will make 256, the price being<span class='line-break'> </span>$140 (one hundred and forty dollars) for the lot com<span class='line-break'></span>plete, and I will send you a template which<span class='line-break'> </span>the bolts on the handles are to fit, and which<span class='line-break'> </span>you can hand to Messrs. Bowker Torrey &amp; Co to drill<span class='line-break'> </span>the holes in the marble doors by, as soon as you are through.<span class='line-break'> </span>I shall want the template returned to me.</p>
<p>As soon as finished send the handles to me at<span class='line-break'> </span>the Cemetery by Emerson's Watertown Express.</p>
<p>Yours truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt.</p>
</div>

<div id="page-1153404">
<h3><a name="page-1153404">CB05_0166</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>166</p>
<p>June 12<sup>th</sup> [187]6</p>
<p>Sam.<sup>l</sup> Batchelder Jr. Esq<span class='line-break'> </span>Secy.&amp;c.</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>I have your favor of June 9<sup>th</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>in regards to photographs by M<sup>r</sup> Black.</p>
<p>As I understand, the person who represents M<sup>r</sup> Black<span class='line-break'> </span>wants not only the lots &amp; places of interest but the<span class='line-break'> </span><u>addresses</u> of the proprietors. I think it was the sense<span class='line-break'> </span>of the Trustees when I first came here that I<span class='line-break'> </span>should not furnish any addresses to any persons<span class='line-break'> </span>who desired to do any work in the Cemetery, and al<span class='line-break'></span>though I at first gave the agents some encouragement<span class='line-break'> </span>I do not, on thinking the matter over, feel at liberty to<span class='line-break'> </span>furnish any addresses.</p>
<p>Any assistance that I can give M<sup>r</sup> Black which<span class='line-break'> </span>it is proper I should do, I shall give with pelasure.<span class='line-break'> </span>As I have received no letters from him, I have sent<span class='line-break'> </span>him none, leaving you as you know him, to<span class='line-break'> </span>make such explanation as you think best. If you<span class='line-break'> </span>think it is worth while you can consult the Pre.<sup>t</sup></p>
<p>Yrs truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering</p>
</div>
</div>

<p>The plan enclosed shows the joints in the slate work<span class='line-break'> </span>above &amp; below the belt course of marble, which should break<span class='line-break'> </span>joints with the slate, and be in at least as long pieces.<span class='line-break'> </span>I shall want the belt course delivered by July 18<sup>th</sup> and<span class='line-break'> </span>the catacombs done ready by August 15<sup>th</sup>.</p>

M<sup>c</sup>Gann will make the handles and I have<span class='line-break'> </span>sent him a template to fit the bolts on handle to which<span class='line-break'> </span>he will have you to drill the holes by. <h3><a name="page-1153420">CB05_0182</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>June 26 [187]6</p>
<p>C. McArthur Esq<span class='line-break'> </span>Foreman</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>On the New<span class='line-break'> </span>Receiving Tomb I as now think it<span class='line-break'> </span>is necessary to increase the width<span class='line-break'> </span>of the side walls, but I consider<span class='line-break'> </span>it also lately necessary that as<span class='line-break'> </span>soon as you reach the spring of<span class='line-break'> </span>the amt. the course should be<span class='line-break'> </span>inclined to the center of that post<span class='line-break'> </span>of the area in which they are.<span class='line-break'> </span>Also that the filling in the area<span class='line-break'> </span>of this side could be vacuumed<span class='line-break'> </span>&amp; same thoroughly saturated with<span class='line-break'> </span>water from the hose when put<span class='line-break'> </span>in.</p>
<p>Yours very truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering Supt.</p>
</div>

<div id="page-1153421">
<h3><a name="page-1153421">CB05_0183</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>183</p>
<p>June 26^th^ [187]6.</p>
<p>Henry C. Davis Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>In reply to your letter of the 24^th^<span class='line-break'> </span>inst I would say that I know of no way in which<span class='line-break'> </span>plastering can be put on a tomb, which is at<span class='line-break'> </span>all durable. I think the plastering cannot be removed neatly.<span class='line-break'> </span>For a new tomb I should  recommend using [face?]<span class='line-break'> </span>brick, but this could not be used on your tomb<span class='line-break'> </span>without building the vestibule and that would be<span class='line-break'> </span>expensive.</p>
<p>I have never seen any marble used, but should think<span class='line-break'> </span>possibly it might be used as a lining; I should think<span class='line-break'> </span>the expense of this would be about $450. I think you<span class='line-break'> </span>could probably get this done cheapest by going directly<span class='line-break'> </span>to one of the large marble [fe..?] in Boston. If I can<span class='line-break'> </span>assist you in any way I will do so with pleasure.</p>
<p>Yours very truly</p>
<p>J.W. Lovering Supt.</p>
</div>
</div>

<p>June [27?]. [6]<span class='line-break'> </span>Miss H.I. Thurston<span class='line-break'> </span>Dear [Madams?]<span class='line-break'> </span>On Saturday last<span class='line-break'> </span>in passing your lot I was suspicious<span class='line-break'> </span>to find some workmen engaged in <span class='line-break'> </span>removing a tree. As they are not <span class='line-break'> </span>allowed to remove trees without <span class='line-break'> </span>permission I spoke to them about it, <span class='line-break'> </span>and they said you [had?] obtained <span class='line-break'> </span>permission and directed them to <span class='line-break'> </span>remove the tree.</p>
<p>Will you be kind enough to give <span class='line-break'> </span>me the facts and also tell [?] to <span class='line-break'> </span>when, if at all, you applied for<span class='line-break'> </span>permission to remove the tree.</p>

<div id="page-1153424">
<h3><a name="page-1153424">CB05_0186</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>186</p>
<p>June 29 [187]6</p>
<p>Mrs. C.C. Andrews</p>
<p>Dear Madam<span class='line-break'> </span>[5 &amp;? Dwight?] So. B.</p>
<p>Your letter of [even? date?] herewith is<span class='line-break'> </span>this moment received. I can have the two graves<span class='line-break'> </span>mounded, and planted with myrtle, as you request<span class='line-break'> </span>but must strongly advise against mounding for<span class='line-break'> </span>various reasons. This manner of planting is<span class='line-break'> </span>very uncommon. It would be, almost, impossible<span class='line-break'> </span>to make myrtle so planted live because in a dry<span class='line-break'> </span>time the mound would be the first part of the<span class='line-break'> </span>surface to dry up, and this plant needs moisture<span class='line-break'> </span>to thrive, again after a year or two the growth of the<span class='line-break'> </span>myrtle would assume the form of, a mound.</p>
<p>We always prepare the ground by enriching it [&amp;c?]<span class='line-break'> </span>and plant the myrtle on a flat surface. To properly<span class='line-break'> </span>prepare &amp; put in the myrtle will cost $7.00 per grave.</p>
<p>This I can have done very soon after receiving<span class='line-break'> </span>your decision.</p>
<p>Very Respectfully</p>
<p>J.W. Lovering Supt.<span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs</p>
</div>
</div>

<p>July 14 [187]6</p>
<p>Mr. H.B. Mackintosh Treas^r^.</p>

<p>Yesterday I received a call<span class='line-break'> </span>from Mrs. L.A. Schirmer Lot 3446 present address<span class='line-break'> </span>42 Newbury St. B. She wished a myrtle grave<span class='line-break'> </span>changed, myrtle repaired, plants set out &amp; the lot cared<span class='line-break'> </span>for and also care of plants for 1877 &amp; bill for both sent<span class='line-break'> </span>to her so she could pay them.</p>
<p>I enclose to you the bill for 1876 &amp; 1877.</p>
<p>If you have unpaid charges, as I think you<span class='line-break'> </span>have, please render to her a bill for all and<span class='line-break'> </span>send [underlined] me a copy of the whole bill, as it is<span class='line-break'> </span>more than likely that she may come here<span class='line-break'> </span>to pay &amp; not bring bill with her.</p>
<p>I have an order to continue care of plants<span class='line-break'> </span>until forbid. If the payment is made to you please advise<span class='line-break'> </span>me of the fact.</p>

<p>J.W.Lovering Sup^t^.<span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs</p>
<p>July 21 [187]6</p>
<p>Mr. Allan F. Boone</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>I have looked<span class='line-break'> </span>at Lot 2442 as requested.<span class='line-break'> </span>To raise all the steps &amp; platform<span class='line-break'> </span>will cost $20.00.</p>
<p>To raise lower step will cost<span class='line-break'> </span>$12.00. The first way is the one<span class='line-break'> </span>I should advise.</p>
<p>There is no way I know of<span class='line-break'> </span>whereby the water can be prevented<span class='line-break'> </span>from standing on the path for a short time<span class='line-break'> </span>after a hard shower. A [cesspool?] to<span class='line-break'> </span>be of any service must be large &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>therefore expensive, and that even would<span class='line-break'> </span>not always insure dryness after heavy<span class='line-break'> </span>showers, say like those of yesterday.</p>
<p>Very Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J W Lovering Sup^t^.<span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs</p>

<div id="page-1153444">
<h3><a name="page-1153444">CB05_0202</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>202</p>
<p>July 28^th^ [187]6</p>
<p>H.S. Grew Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Your favor of July 26^th rec'd. I have examined<span class='line-break'> </span>the tomb carefully and fail to find anything the matter<span class='line-break'> </span>with the granite. The granite was washed off the first<span class='line-break'> </span>of the week, probably since you heard from Miss Sturgis.</p>
<p>I went to the tomb with her on Monday I think. Nothing<span class='line-break'> </span>was said there about the granite or marble. The tiles which<span class='line-break'> </span>are newly set are not yet thoroughly dry and the moisture<span class='line-break'> </span>in the cement had spread from them a little way up<span class='line-break'> </span>the marble front. This will dry out in time, and if<span class='line-break'> </span>the tiles need it they can be washed off again<span class='line-break'> </span>when dry. I do not like to set tiles without cement or<span class='line-break'> </span>lime in a tomb, and yet find in almost every lot<span class='line-break'> </span>of tiles set, that some become somewhat discolored.</p>
<p>I expect to come to Mt Desert by the Lewiston tonight &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>if you desire further conversation on the subject, you will<span class='line-break'> </span>find me for a day or two at The Rockaway House or if you<span class='line-break'> </span>will let me know, I will call on you.</p>
<p>Yours truly</p>
<p>J.W. Lovering.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />

<p>Aug 7^th^. [187]6</p>
<p>Geo. H. Chickering Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>The terms of the sale of the<span class='line-break'> </span>ornamental addition to your lot have been<span class='line-break'> </span>carefully considered, but the Committee on Lots feel that they have<span class='line-break'> </span>already made a considerable concession in selling you<span class='line-break'> </span>an ornamental land at a lower rate, land which is<span class='line-break'> </span>entirely suitable, and as readily sold as usual, for<span class='line-break'> </span>a burial lot, which makes a difference in the amount<span class='line-break'> </span>received by us of $234. -- and this they did because<span class='line-break'> </span>you had done so much to make your lot an [attrac<span class='line-break'></span>tive? one?]. The other lots have been sold with the under<span class='line-break'></span>standing that every lot on the new territory was to be under<span class='line-break'> </span>[?] care and the trustees passed a vote to this effect<span class='line-break'> </span>[?] any sales were [?] which they do not see that<span class='line-break'> </span>[?].</p>
<p>I would call your attention to the fact that all the price<span class='line-break'> </span>[?] that [now?] and are much lower than in the old Cemetery<span class='line-break'> </span>and [?] a deduction was made to you by your taking<span class='line-break'> </span>the land as ornamental land. I wrote you to this effect in June<span class='line-break'> </span>&amp; think the letter must have miscarried -- Respectfully J.W. Lovering</p>

<h3><a name="page-1153452">CB05_0211</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>211</p>
<p>Aug 7^th^. [187]6.</p>
<p>Geo. H. Stone Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>When you purchased lot #4318 some<span class='line-break'> </span>two years ago the lot was rough graded posted &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>numbered for which a charge of $54.00 was made<span class='line-break'> </span>which was specified on the memo of sale sent you<span class='line-break'> </span>and to which no objection was made at the time.<span class='line-break'> </span>In April 1875 I wrote you a note explaining the<span class='line-break'> </span>charge, in answer I believe, to one sent to the Treasurer<span class='line-break'> </span>of the Corporation by you.</p>
<p>Several weeks ago, Miss Stone, I think, inquired the<span class='line-break'> </span>cost of sodding the lot and was informed $36 which with<span class='line-break'> </span>the original charge of $54.00 would make $90 as low a<span class='line-break'> </span>price as is ever charged for the grading sodding &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>posting of the lots of this size.</p>
<p>I think both for your sake and ours the lot should be<span class='line-break'> </span>completed &amp; put in good order, and if you are here at any<span class='line-break'> </span>time, I think I can readily satisfy you that both charges<span class='line-break'> </span>are fair &amp; just ones. The sodding of the lot, I shall wait to hear from <span class='line-break'> </span>you about, and I hope you will settle the charge of $54 without<span class='line-break'> </span>more delay.</p>
<p>Yours very truly</p>
<p>J.W. Lovering Supt.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>

The<span class='line-break'> </span>size of this lot would be 150 sq feet (one half the <span class='line-break'> </span>usual size) and the price of this lot finished ready<span class='line-break'> </span>for use with corner posts, numbered, and sodded,<span class='line-break'> </span>including also the care of the grass forever, would<span class='line-break'> </span>be ( $435 [/100?] ) four hundred and thirty five dollars.<span class='line-break'> </span>There are some lots a little farther from the<span class='line-break'> </span>Entrance, of about the same size which we can <span class='line-break'> </span>sell you for $300, and although there is not very<span class='line-break'> </span>much shade there now, we are likely to set out<span class='line-break'> </span>more trees this fall &amp; next spring.</p>
