<h3><a name="page-1153473">CB05_0232</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>232</p>
<p>Sept. 4 [187]6.</p>
<p>J.M. Spelman Esq<span class='line-break'> </span>Prest.</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>All fees received for use of the<span class='line-break'> </span>New Receiving Tomb. are to be divided according to<span class='line-break'> </span>agreement with the Horticultural Society, they receiving<span class='line-break'> </span>one-fourth.</p>
<p>I think the rates now changed should be altered<span class='line-break'> </span>in order to simply the matter of dividing the fees, and<span class='line-break'> </span>to get a proper compensation for use of the tomb.</p>
<p>The present charge is $25.00 in advance, of which $17.00<span class='line-break'> </span>is refunded if the body is removed <u>to a lot</u> within four<span class='line-break'> </span>months, leaving $8.00 to cover the Expense of use of tomb,<span class='line-break'> </span>removal of body and interment in lot. If from the Cemetery, no [return?].</p>
<p>If the body remains over four months no return is made,<span class='line-break'> </span>but after proper notice to the friends of the deceased, if<span class='line-break'> </span>the body is not removed by them, it is placed in the<span class='line-break'> </span>Receiving Tomb Lot, with out Extra charge.</p>
<p>On the following sheet you will find the rate <span class='line-break'> </span>[?] at other places.</p>
</div>

<div id="page-1153475">
<h3><a name="page-1153475">CB05_0234</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>234</p>
<p>3)</p>
<p>I would suggest that the following rates, be changed, if<span class='line-break'> </span>they meet the approval of the Trustees.</p>
<p>For the deposit of any body $20. in advance and<span class='line-break'> </span>after three months $4.00 for each month or part of a month.<span class='line-break'> </span>The usual fee for interments $5.00 to be charged for<span class='line-break'> </span>the^deposit in and^ removal of Each body from the tomb, and into inter<span class='line-break'></span>ment in a lot, with the necessary records.</p>
<p>After a body has remained in the tomb for 3 [mns?] it<span class='line-break'> </span>will be removed to the Receiving Tomb Lot unless a deposit<span class='line-break'> </span>is made for an additional time as above.</p>
<p>Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering</p>
</div>
</div>

<p>Your postal card of Sep^r^ 8<span class='line-break'> </span>is received. We have no printed prospectus<span class='line-break'> </span>or advertisement.</p>
<p>For a certain sum of money (fixed at the discretion<span class='line-break'> </span>of the Trustees and of course varying with the value of<span class='line-break'> </span>the improvements on the lots and the probably expense<span class='line-break'> </span>of maintaining them &amp; the lot in best of order) the Trustees<span class='line-break'> </span>give a guaranty contract to keep such lot forever<span class='line-break'> </span>in like good order as when taken together with such<span class='line-break'> </span>monumental structures as may at that time be<span class='line-break'> </span>upon the lot. Or a person may deposit<span class='line-break'> </span>with the Treas^r^ any sum of money exceeding<span class='line-break'> </span>say $100.^00^ the interest whereof will be used to keep<span class='line-break'> </span>the lot in repair but the Trustees do not of course agree<span class='line-break'> </span>that the said interest shall be sufficient to properly<span class='line-break'> </span>keep the lot in order. <p>Sept 14 [187]6</p>
<p>[F.W. Greigg?] Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>I make the superficial measurement of<span class='line-break'> </span>the floor of the New Receiving Tomb very nearly 800 sq feet<span class='line-break'> </span>which you can verify from the measures taken by you.<span class='line-break'> </span>I have put in a foundation of small stone 3 feet deep,<span class='line-break'> </span>and I propose to level this with concrete to a surface<span class='line-break'> </span>[depth?] of an inch below the top of the tiles.</p>
<p>I will give you $600 (six hundred dollars) to furnish<span class='line-break'> </span>the tile repairs by Mr Wellington and have him lay<span class='line-break'> </span>them in Portland cement in the most thorough and<span class='line-break'> </span>careful manner, and to guarantee the work.</p>
<p>This price is intended to cover the whole cost of furnishing<span class='line-break'> </span>&amp; laying including packing, delivering, waste, [fees?] &amp;c.</p>
<p>Yours very truly</p>
<p>J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>Sup.^t^</p>

<p>Upon making<span class='line-break'> </span>inquiry I find that all the<span class='line-break'> </span>grave borders are on the lot now<span class='line-break'> </span>that have ever been there, so far<span class='line-break'> </span>as anyone here recollects --</p>
<p>I think the lady is under<span class='line-break'> </span>misapprehension as to the original<span class='line-break'> </span>number</p>
<p>Very Respectfully</p>
<p>J.W. Lovering Sup^t^.<span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs</p>
<p>Oct 3 [187]6</p>
<p>Franklin Snow Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>The myrtle<span class='line-break'> </span>will be planted on the 3 small<span class='line-break'> </span>graves as you direct in your<span class='line-break'> </span>letter of yesterday in the course<span class='line-break'> </span>of two or three days</p>
<p>Very Respectfully</p>
<p>J.W. Lovering Sup^t^.<span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs</p>

[Litley?], the representative<span class='line-break'> </span>of Lot #1923 (containing 300 sq feet) on Acacia path, desires<span class='line-break'> </span>to purchase a lot on the Stone Farm, provided the corpora<span class='line-break'></span>tion will take his present lot in part payment.</p>

<div id="page-1153493">
<h3><a name="page-1153493">CB05_0252</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>252</p>
<p>Oct. 7 [187]6</p>
<p>Hanson Bigelow Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Your favor of yesterday<span class='line-break'> </span>enclosing my letter of <span class='line-break'> </span>3^d^ inst to Mr. Snow Is received.</p>
<p>I have been to the lot this morning and find<span class='line-break'> </span>no evidence of there ever having been the grave marks<span class='line-break'> </span>there, the want of which occasioned the complaint</p>
<p>In the case where grave borders are now there, the<span class='line-break'> </span>base stone of the headstones was cut to receive the ends, but<span class='line-break'> </span>the base at the grave that has no borders, appears never<span class='line-break'> </span>to have been so cut. Upon inquiry I find that none<span class='line-break'> </span>of the employees here, most likely to know, recollect<span class='line-break'> </span>any border at all at that grave. I am therefore<span class='line-break'> </span>constrained to believe that the lady had supposed<span class='line-break'> </span>a border where in fact none was ever placed; which<span class='line-break'> </span>might readily happen from a slip of memory</p>
<p>Very Respectfully</p>
<p>J.W. Lovering Sup.^t^<span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs</p>
</div>
</div>

Tyler deceased proprietor of which<span class='line-break'> </span>you are Representative. The Representative<span class='line-break'> </span>cannot give legal title if any other<span class='line-break'> </span>heirs exist and, in case there are no<span class='line-break'> </span>other heirs he ceases to be Rep. and becomes<span class='line-break'> </span>sole heir or owner; so that, unless you<span class='line-break'> </span>can obtain the signatures of all the<span class='line-break'> </span>heirs to the deed of reconveyance, it <span class='line-break'> </span>appears that nothing can be done.</p>

<p>On the 10<sup>th</sup> day of November 1873 I received from<span class='line-break'> </span>you an order to take annual care of lot 4271 with plants<span class='line-break'> </span>and top dressing until further ordered. These directions<span class='line-break'> </span>I have executed up to this date - This year (1876) Care and<span class='line-break'> </span>plants at an expense of $7.00; the top dressing would have<span class='line-break'> </span>been put on about November 1<sup>st</sup> at a cost of $3.00 -</p>
<p>Am I correct in supposing that the postal card is an <span class='line-break'> </span>order to stop all work on the lot on &amp; after this date?</p>

<h3><a name="page-1153505">CB05_0264</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>264</p>
<p>4 - P.M.<span class='line-break'> </span>Oct 19 [187]6</p>
<p>Mr. L.A. Roberts</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>The lot that<span class='line-break'> </span>you looked at no. 3221 Yew A.<span class='line-break'> </span>was shown to a gentleman last<span class='line-break'> </span>evening, he was not fully<span class='line-break'> </span>decided but we told him<span class='line-break'> </span>that he could have the lot<span class='line-break'> </span>at a moments notice, if, unsold<span class='line-break'> </span>at the time. Therefore I cannot<span class='line-break'> </span>hold it for you as proposed.</p>
<p>It stands thus -- he who first<span class='line-break'> </span>notifies us, by whose notice we<span class='line-break'> </span>first receive, takes the lot.<span class='line-break'> </span>To this date &amp; time nothing has<span class='line-break'> </span>been heard from the other party --</p>
<p>Please advise</p>
<p>Very Respectfully</p>
<p>J W Lovering Sup.^t^<span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs</p>
</div>
</div>

<p>Oct 21 [187]6</p>
<p>Mrs. Newell H. [Moulton?]</p>
<p>Dear Madam</p>
<p>On the 6<sup>th</sup> day of Sep<sup>t</sup> I<span class='line-break'> </span>[wrote?] to you asking permission to<span class='line-break'> </span>change the grade of your lot<span class='line-break'> </span>3439 in order to improve the general<span class='line-break'> </span>appearance of that part of the<span class='line-break'> </span>Cemetery where we were making<span class='line-break'> </span>some changes. As yet I have<span class='line-break'> </span>heard no response. The other parties<span class='line-break'> </span>to whom I applied have given me<span class='line-break'> </span>the necessary permission, with<span class='line-break'> </span>the exception of Mrs Brown to whom<span class='line-break'> </span>I have again written today -</p>
<p>Please give this matter the attention<span class='line-break'> </span>it merits as soon as possible, in <span class='line-break'> </span>order that the work may be done<span class='line-break'> </span>this fall Very Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. <p>Oct 27 [187]6</p>
<p>B.B. Converse Esq</p>

<p>Your note of yesterday<span class='line-break'> </span>is received. The bill you return was<span class='line-break'> </span>sent by request. April 16/76 Mr. G.S.<span class='line-break'> </span>C. left an order here for "care" "plants"<span class='line-break'> </span>and "top dressing" as per copy which I<span class='line-break'> </span>enclose. As we graded &amp; sodded your<span class='line-break'> </span>lot this year we made no charge for<span class='line-break'> </span>keepig the sod in order. The plans [?]<span class='line-break'> </span>charge for. As the bill shows, the top dressing<span class='line-break'> </span>is to be [?] on about Nov. 1. I think it <span class='line-break'> </span>advisable to top dress the sod this fall, but<span class='line-break'> </span>as it has not yet been done I can cancel<span class='line-break'> </span>the order therefor If you so direct</p>
<p>I ought to be advised of your wishes<span class='line-break'> </span>immediately</p>
<p>Very Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering Sup<sup>t</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>Per Childs</p>
<p>Oct 28 [187]6</p>
<p>Mr. C.C. Thayer</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Your favor of<span class='line-break'> </span>Oct 26 was received this a.m. by which<span class='line-break'> </span>I understand that you wish the same care<span class='line-break'> </span>&amp;c, as formerly charged to Miss Thayer.</p>
<p>The myrtle or periwinkle is put on a<span class='line-break'> </span>flat surface after the ground is prepared<span class='line-break'> </span>for it and forms a slight mound by<span class='line-break'> </span>its own growth in due time.</p>
<p>This I will have placed on the grave<span class='line-break'> </span>in the spring, which is the best time for<span class='line-break'> </span>the purpose</p>
<p>Very Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering Sup<sup>t</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs</p>

<div class="page-content">
<p>280</p>
<p>Nov 16 [187]6</p>
<p>Henry Woods Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>In reply to your favor of Nov 3<sup>rd</sup>, I would<span class='line-break'> </span>say that I have visited your lot, and think a set of steps<span class='line-break'> </span>would be a considerable advantage to the lot. I would not<span class='line-break'> </span>advise any other stonework except perhaps more ornamental<span class='line-break'> </span>posts to mark the lot.</p>
<p>The ornamental posts of granite are worth from $20 to $25 each<span class='line-break'> </span>and you would require 4 on the corners and 1 to mark the<span class='line-break'> </span>division line between #[2654?] and #2266</p>
<p>The steps would be 5 in number, with buttresses and names<span class='line-break'> </span>&amp; numbers of both lots are there with 5 plain steps, buttresses &amp; <span class='line-break'> </span>posts on are, or with the [?] posts at entrance<span class='line-break'> </span>and plan buttresses the cost would be about $155 if a [Rockham?]<span class='line-break'> </span>Granite; with posts at top and between [?] steps the cost would<span class='line-break'> </span>be $205 for Rockport granite, and are somewhat less if of<span class='line-break'> </span>Concord or [?] Granite. These prices are in addition to the<span class='line-break'> </span>cost of setting which would be from $30 to $60 according to the<span class='line-break'> </span>style. If you [?] for the stone, delivered at the lot, the corpo<span class='line-break'></span>ration will set the work for you. The corporation [?] furnish the<span class='line-break'> </span>stone work, according to the regulations of the Trustees <span class='line-break'> </span>Ys truly J.W. Lovering</p>

You are charged now<span class='line-break'> </span>3628 - 770 sq. ft. $6.00 + flowers $4.00 = 10.00<span class='line-break'> </span>3629 880 " " 6.00 = " 4.00 10.00</p>

<div id="page-1153550">
<h3><a name="page-1153550">CB05_0309</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>309</p>
<p>Dec 12<sup>th</sup> [187]6.</p>
<p>J.M. Spelman. Prest.</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Enclosed please find plans for widening<span class='line-break'> </span>the bridge at Auburn Lake from sixteen to forty four feet<span class='line-break'> </span>which will cost with all necessary grading, $625.<sup>00</sup></p>
<p>I have also Examined into the probable cost of<span class='line-break'> </span>widening the present path around the upper end of the<span class='line-break'> </span>lake into an avenue sixteen feet wide. I find the average<span class='line-break'> </span>depth of water in the lake to be four feet, and that the bottom<span class='line-break'> </span>is [mud?] to a depth of from 3 to 6 feet more.</p>
<p>Probably 4000 yards of filling would be required to<span class='line-break'> </span>build the avenue, the cost of moving which from any part<span class='line-break'> </span>of the Cemetery could not be less than $1000, and at present<span class='line-break'> </span>it would not seem to me that there is that amount of<span class='line-break'> </span>material to spare. If material is bought for the [?], it will<span class='line-break'> </span>cost as much as six hundred dollars more. Beyond this will be<span class='line-break'> </span>the cost of regrading &amp; sodding the banks, which after deducting<span class='line-break'> </span>the value of stone taken out would be four or five hundred<span class='line-break'> </span>dollars, and finally as the avenue is narrow, and the distances<span class='line-break'> </span>between it &amp; the lake [?] it might be necessary to protect [positions?]<span class='line-break'> </span>by a railway Respectfully J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />

<p>Dec 14 6</p>
<p>Mr. W. Appleton  76 Beacon St. B.</p>
<p>Dear Sir,</p>
<p>The difficulty<span class='line-break'> </span>in the matter of the slab is to get<span class='line-break'> </span>so large, a stone of proper<span class='line-break'> </span>size free, of blemish, in splitting<span class='line-break'> </span>one from the quary.</p>
<p>The foundation, in the lot was prepared<span class='line-break'> </span>som time since and is covered with<span class='line-break'> </span>straw protected so that the slab<span class='line-break'> </span>can be placed on it at any time.</p>

<div id="page-1153554">
<h3><a name="page-1153554">CB05_0313</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>313</p>
<p>December 18th 6.</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>When I came into office I was informed that the hay<span class='line-break'> </span>and by your end had always been allowed to you from<span class='line-break'> </span>what was [cut?] by the Corporation.</p>
<p>As you are [?] aware, the opportunities [for?] cutting<span class='line-break'> </span>hay are smaller  now than in former years on assessment of<span class='line-break'> </span>the [amount?] of the Cemetery, and in 1874 the corporation was<span class='line-break'> </span>obliged to bring in hay, and again this year I expect to have<span class='line-break'> </span>to do so, and in [view?] of these facts, I fell <u>obliged</u> to notify<span class='line-break'> </span>you that hereafter you must furnish your own hay.</p>
<p>The barn appeared to me last summer to be as [even?]<span class='line-break'> </span>filled as usual, and as the hay lasted this 1875. I do<span class='line-break'> </span>not quite see why we should be so short now, and it has<span class='line-break'> </span>remained to me that you may have borrowed for your heard<span class='line-break'> </span>intending to replace it. I wish you would let me know<span class='line-break'> </span>whether this is the case or not, and if it is how much you <span class='line-break'> </span>have used.</p>
<p>If not, can you suggest any reason why the amount should<span class='line-break'> </span>seem short, as from your previous experience with the same<span class='line-break'> </span>stick you know about what is required. I desire a written reply.</p>
<p>A. A. Barker Es.</p>
<p>Yr very truly J. W. Lovering Supt.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />

<h3><a name="page-1153556">CB05_0315</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>315</p>
<p>Dec. 19. 6</p>
<p>Joseph Collins Esq</p>
<p>Dr Sir</p>
<p>Now that I have put<span class='line-break'> </span>one man in charge of the barn I<span class='line-break'> </span>want to make a new arrangement as<span class='line-break'> </span>to repair of wagon, harnesses or shoeing.</p>
<p>I have directed Mr. McArthur to keep<span class='line-break'> </span>your wagon harness &amp; the house which may<span class='line-break'> </span>reassigned for your use in order, that<span class='line-break'> </span>you may have no delay when you want<span class='line-break'> </span>him.</p>
<p>In case any repairs are needed you<span class='line-break'> </span>will apply to him on to me, as I shall<span class='line-break'> </span>make a new arrangement with him <span class='line-break'> </span>as to the parties with whom to deal for<span class='line-break'> </span>repairs.</p>
<p>Yours very truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J. W. Lovering Supt.</p>
<p>Dec 19th 6.</p>
<p>C. McArthur Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Now that we have one<span class='line-break'> </span>man in charge of the barn, I expect <span class='line-break'> </span>him to see that all wagons &amp; horses belonging<span class='line-break'> </span>to the corporation are kept ready for use.</p>
<p>You will take the entire charge of all<span class='line-break'> </span>the shoeing to be done. Keeping such a<span class='line-break'> </span>record as will be necessary to check off<span class='line-break'> </span>the likes by. Also, you will have any needed<span class='line-break'> </span>repairs made promptly, which may be<span class='line-break'> </span>needed on the harness. The larger ones<span class='line-break'> </span>I wish you come consult me about.</p>
<p>This includes the herse &amp; wagon owned<span class='line-break'> </span>by the gardener, and I want this kept<span class='line-break'> </span>ready for use without delay to him<span class='line-break'> </span>at such times of year as he needs it.</p>
<p>Your truly</p>
<p>J. W. Lovering Supt.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>

<div class="page-content">
<p>317</p>
<p>Dec 26  6</p>
<p>E. Johnson Esq.</p>
<p>Dear Sir.</p>
<p>I have made a careful inquiry as to<span class='line-break'> </span>the removal of the flower frames &amp; done from your lot<span class='line-break'> </span>and are convinced that no employee of the corporation<span class='line-break'> </span>is in any way concerned.</p>
<p>The first often come out &amp; remove the forget frames<span class='line-break'> </span>and I think that it is quite possible that it occurred<span class='line-break'> </span>in the way. I did not understand you to say when<span class='line-break'> </span>I saw you Saturday, that you have seen the florists<span class='line-break'> </span>and if you have not, it might be worth while.</p>
<p>I will keep the matter in mixed &amp; will seem you would<span class='line-break'> </span>if I learn anything once, as if the remain was made by<span class='line-break'> </span>any [?] [?], it is the intent of the corporation<span class='line-break'> </span>as well as your own, to do all [p?] to prevent it.</p>
<p>Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J. W. Lovering</p>
</div>

<div id="page-1153565">
<h3><a name="page-1153565">CB05_0324</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>324</p>
<p>3)</p>
<p>Fountain Ave has been raised and put in good condition<span class='line-break'> </span>from the gate at the Engine house to Central Ave, and the<span class='line-break'> </span>land in rear of New Receiving Tomb has been graded, with<span class='line-break'> </span>a little more work here these will be 20 desirable 300 ft lots.<span class='line-break'> </span>----------------------<span class='line-break'></span>On the Stone Farm the lots between Eagle &amp; Swan Ave's (90<span class='line-break'> </span>in number) are graded &amp; sodded complete, some are already<span class='line-break'> </span>posted and posts are on hand for a portion of the balance.</p>
<p>With some of the surplus earth on a portion of this farm, the land<span class='line-break'> </span>near the East Gate^(or Engine house gate on Coolidge Ave)^ which was previously [?] and wet has<span class='line-break'> </span>been raised so that there is 1/3 of an acre which can<span class='line-break'> </span>be used for lots when desired, which would make some 30<span class='line-break'> </span>lots.</p>
<p>The avenue running from East Gate parallel with Coolidge<span class='line-break'> </span>Ave, is now <del>complete</del> graded for the whole length of the fence<span class='line-break'> </span>line, and the land between the avenue &amp; fence has been<span class='line-break'> </span>graded and sown with grass seed, and trees have been<span class='line-break'> </span>set out.</p>
<p>On the stone farm, around Halcyon Lake &amp; elsewhere 751<span class='line-break'> </span>trees have been set out and a few shrubs.</p>
<p>About 170 trees have been cut during the year, for the most part<span class='line-break'> </span>along the fence line on Mt. Auburn Street. (Over)<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>

<h3><a name="page-1153567">CB05_0326</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>326</p>
<p>4/</p>
<p>New Rec. Tomb.</p>
<p>is complete except the tiling of the floor, and in addition<span class='line-break'> </span>to the amount already charged in this years a/c will be some<span class='line-break'> </span>$750 or $800 more which will make the probable cost $9509.93/800=10,339.93-</p>
<p>The tomb contains 128 catacombs, largest 3' x 2' - smallest 37" x 20"<span class='line-break'> </span>------------------------<span class='line-break'></span>During the year the filling of the low part of Spruce Ave with<span class='line-break'> </span>stone has continued - so that now for 200 feet on each side<span class='line-break'> </span>of the Ave, the stone has been filled 3 to 4 ft wide and from 6 to<span class='line-break'> </span>8 feet deep. below the [?] of clay which underlies this whole<span class='line-break'> </span>territory. This [hollow?] received the surface drainage of 16 acres.</p>
<p>The fall rains soaked away as fast as they fell, and several^(5)^<span class='line-break'> </span>cesspools have been put in which connect with the broken<span class='line-break'> </span>stone and [?] the water thru' the stone -</p>
<p>Several other ^(20)^ cesspools have been put in connecting with the<span class='line-break'> </span>drains already built, in [low?] places where the water has<span class='line-break'> </span>accumulated on the avenues and frequently caused much<span class='line-break'> </span>inconvenience, as well as damage by washing - and<span class='line-break'> </span>gutters have been [pared?] (3297) feet in the [?].</p>
<p>There is already a noticable reduction in the labor of repairing<span class='line-break'> </span>[?] avenues after [storms?]</p>
<p>Respectfuly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering</p>
</div>

<p>I have received a letter<span class='line-break'> </span>from Col Warren accepting your offer of<span class='line-break'> </span>$300 for lot #382 on Narcissus Path.</p>
<p>He has sent on the deed with a<span class='line-break'> </span>transfer to you by Wells Fargo &amp; Co, &amp; their<span class='line-break'> </span>treasurer notified us yesterday of the receipt<span class='line-break'> </span>of the papers in Boston.</p>
<p>Col. Warren wrote me to have the remains<span class='line-break'> </span>of his sons formerly interred in the lot,<span class='line-break'> </span>removed &amp; forwarded to him by Wells Fargo &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>Co., but they, not understanding about this,<span class='line-break'> </span>have declined to receive them, without <span class='line-break'> </span>further instructions from San Francisco &amp; have<span class='line-break'> </span>sent for them. This will cause some little<span class='line-break'> </span>delay. The remains have been removed from <span class='line-break'> </span>the lot, and as soon as Wells Fargo &amp; Co take them,<span class='line-break'> </span>the transfer can be made of the title.</p>

<div class="page-content">
<p>338</p>
<p>Jan'y 31 [187]7</p>
<p>Mr. Geo. H. Jones</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Your postal C/ received<span class='line-break'> </span>There are two ways, the first most common way<span class='line-break'> </span>is to deposit with the Treas.^r^ a fixed sum named<span class='line-break'> </span>by the Trustees after examination of the lot; in this case<span class='line-break'> </span>the sum would probably be not more than $500.<span class='line-break'> </span>This sum presupposes the lot placed in best order at an<span class='line-break'> </span>additional expense of whatever may be necessary in the way of sod<span class='line-break'></span>ding &amp;c. The Corporation give a guaranty contract to forever<span class='line-break'> </span>keep the lot in like good order as when taken -- or</p>
<p>You can pay into the hands of the Treasurer<span class='line-break'> </span>any sum over $100. which the Corp^n^ will invest &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>spend the interest yearly in keeping the lot in good order</p>
<p>This is however not so satisfactory a way as<span class='line-break'> </span>the other to the Proprietor. If you wish &amp; think well<span class='line-break'> </span>of the price named I can have the lot examined in<span class='line-break'> </span>the spring &amp; have you notified of the sum fixed</p>
<p>Very Respectfully</p>
<p>J.W. Lovering Sup.^t^<span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs</p>

<div class="page-content">
<p>347</p>
<p>Feby 10 [187]7</p>
<p>Mr. G.H. Richardson 31 Pemberton Sq. B.</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Your favor is received</p>
<p>Annual Care of a lot without plants includes - Cutting<span class='line-break'> </span>grass as often as may be necessary, the number of<span class='line-break'> </span>times varying with the position of the lot and dryness<span class='line-break'> </span>of season from 16 times to 30 times through the growing season<span class='line-break'> </span>it includes watering the plants when needed but does not<span class='line-break'> </span>include watering the grass, a thing which, except on newly<span class='line-break'> </span>sodded lots, is impracticable, in most of the lots, and is<span class='line-break'> </span>very seldom done here, and then, only at an additional cost</p>
<p>The grass, in ordinary seasons keep green &amp; fresh, if care<span class='line-break'> </span>is taken in the cutting. For $250 we put on a top dressing<span class='line-break'> </span>in fall of the very best stable manure that can be bought, of<span class='line-break'> </span>the same quality &amp; quantity that we got $4.00. for in 1875</p>
<p>I do not know the condition of your sod but think<span class='line-break'> </span>you had best give me an order for the care of the lot now<span class='line-break'> </span>so that it may be put in order in early spring and<span class='line-break'> </span>then send me word when you would like to meet</p>
<p>-over-</p>
</div>
</div>

<p>348</p>
<p>our Gardener here who will go to the lot with<span class='line-break'> </span>you and advise with you as to what you wish<span class='line-break'> </span>done.</p>
<p>In ordinary cases as in the 1500 or 1600 lots<span class='line-break'> </span>of 300 sq ft which we take annual care of we find<span class='line-break'> </span>that #3.75 for care &amp; $2.50 Top dressing^per annum^ is ample to<span class='line-break'> </span>keep the lots in good order for a term of years,<span class='line-break'> </span>of course from time to time on an average here<span class='line-break'> </span>of once in 7 years the lots have to be resodded.</p>

I have not seen the<span class='line-break'> </span>gentleman here as yet and as some five<span class='line-break'> </span>months have elapsed (the interment having been<span class='line-break'> </span>made Sep<sup>t</sup>. 27 1876) it would seem that a<span class='line-break'> </span>sufficient time had been aloowed ~ Mr White<span class='line-break'> </span>can call on Mr. J.H. Reed 16 Pemberton Sq the<span class='line-break'> </span>Secretary of the Corporation to arrange the matter<span class='line-break'> </span>if more convenient than to come out here.</p>
<p>Please give this immediate attention</p>
<p>Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering Sup<sup>t</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs<span class='line-break'> </span></p>

Later in May<span class='line-break'> </span>you arranged to have this lot graded &amp; sodded and at that<span class='line-break'> </span>time, desired to have te curbing cleaned better when<span class='line-break'> </span>it was represented that this could not be done except by<span class='line-break'> </span>employing a stone cutter.</p>

<h3><a name="page-1153603">CB05_0359</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>359</p>
<p>Feb'y 26<sup>th</sup> [187]7</p>
<p>Cha<sup>s</sup> L. Bates Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>In regard to the charges on bill<span class='line-break'> </span>for work on your lot, I would say I know of no errors<span class='line-break'> </span>I understand you to claim none</p>
<p>On the bill for grading &amp; sodding Mrs Lockwood's lot<span class='line-break'> </span>(#4417) is an item of 199 loads of loam and this I<span class='line-break'> </span>believe you desire an abatement on.</p>
<p>In selling the lot it was the intention to sell it<span class='line-break'> </span>as you took it, but, as I am inclined to think I made<span class='line-break'> </span>a statement to you which induced you to think<span class='line-break'> </span>that there was a foot of loam on the lot, [?] ornamental<span class='line-break'> </span>grounds (this being the depth to which it is usualy put on)<span class='line-break'> </span>whereas in reality it was only six inches deep, or overhalf<span class='line-break'> </span>of what was represented, I think it is no more than [?]<span class='line-break'> </span>for me to deduct from the bill the amount of [loam?] necessary<span class='line-break'> </span>to bring the depth to the amount stated. This would be<span class='line-break'> </span>46 loads which as charged would amount to $55<sup>20</sup>. I<span class='line-break'> </span>have requested the Treasurer to send you a corrected bill &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>a prompt settlement will much oblige</p>
<p>Yrs <u>truly</u> J.W. Lovering</p>

<p>April 10 [187]7</p>
<p>Mr. H.H. Weeks</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>The sizes are as<span class='line-break'> </span>follows Waist 36 in inside seam of<span class='line-break'> </span>leg 32 1/2</p>
<p>Girth under arms 3 ft. 5 1/2 In.</p>
<p>The sizes do not want to be snug<span class='line-break'> </span>but rather liberal</p>
<p>I think you can fit us<span class='line-break'> </span>out with goods worth about<span class='line-break'> </span>$20 the suit Send by <u>Emersons<span class='line-break'> </span>Express</u> to</p>
<p>J.W. Lovering Sup<sup>t</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs</p>

<p>Your favor of yesterday rec'd,<span class='line-break'> </span>and in reply I would say that a plan can be<span class='line-break'> </span>furnished you for $3<sup>00</sup> and this would include<span class='line-break'> </span>a record of it on our book of plans here.</p>

<p>Your order for flowers on grave 117 lot 3730<span class='line-break'> </span>will not suffer by a short delay as we could<span class='line-break'> </span>not set out plants with safety until about the middle<span class='line-break'> </span>of May. I should advise very [?] against<span class='line-break'> </span>trying to leave the grave mounded as in that<span class='line-break'> </span>case it would in a moderately dry season<span class='line-break'> </span>cause the flowers to dry up [?] of all<span class='line-break'> </span>the care we could exercise. <div class="page-content">
<p>383</p>
<p>April 16 [187]7</p>
<p>Mrs. M.C. Sparke</p>
<p>Dear Madam</p>
<p>The sum of $100.<sup>00</sup> was<span class='line-break'> </span>deposited with the Treasurer of this Corporation and<span class='line-break'> </span>placed to the credit of the Kirkland Mont, the<span class='line-break'> </span><u>interest</u> of which is used for such necessary<span class='line-break'> </span>repairs as from time to time become necessary.</p>
<p>The Corp<sup>n</sup> does not assure any responsibility in<span class='line-break'> </span>the matter whatever, but only agrees to spend the <u>in<span class='line-break'></span>come</u> of the fund, This however is not considered<span class='line-break'> </span>generally a satisfactory way; the more common [are?]<span class='line-break'> </span>the best way, is to pay a certain &amp; fixed sum<span class='line-break'> </span>named by the Trustees upon consideration of the<span class='line-break'> </span>risks &amp;c, for which the Corp<sup>n</sup> assumes the whole<span class='line-break'> </span>care of the lot and structures in it &amp; agrees to<span class='line-break'> </span>forever keep them in like good order as where secured<span class='line-break'> </span>This is called "placing the lot under perpetual repair"</p>
<p>Any further information you may desire I shall<span class='line-break'> </span>be pleased to communicate Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering Sup<sup>t</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs</p>

<p>An interment was made in your tomb April 1<sup>st</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>1877, and instead of being placed in a catacomb as<span class='line-break'> </span>it should have been, was left in the vestibule of the tomb;<span class='line-break'> </span>the rules of the Trustees require that all bodies shall<span class='line-break'> </span>be placed in the catacombs and sealed up.</p>
<p>I request your immediate attention to the above, as<span class='line-break'> </span>the key of the tomb is not here, and especially as complaints<span class='line-break'> </span>have been made that the tomb is offensive</p>
<p>Very respectfuly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering</p>
<p>[Alvan?] Clark Esq<span class='line-break'> </span>184 Brookline St<span class='line-break'> </span>Cambridgeport<span class='line-break'> </span></p>

<h3><a name="page-1153669">CB05_0424</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>421</p>
<p>May 22 [187]7</p>
<p>Rev. George E. Ellis</p>
<p>Dr Sir</p>
<p>Your note of yesterday, in regard to<span class='line-break'> </span>the work on your lot reached me this morning and I have<span class='line-break'> </span>first returned from the lot.</p>
<p>I will have the gate repaired at once; I know it was left<span class='line-break'> </span>in order last year, but either the roots of the tree, or the [frat?] has<span class='line-break'> </span>thrown it out of positions. I do not find anything out of the<span class='line-break'> </span>way with the paint, the iron work being thoroughly covered,<span class='line-break'> </span>and no signs of rust being visible. I think you must refer to<span class='line-break'> </span>the [dullness?] of the paint, and however bright &amp; fresh the fence<span class='line-break'> </span>looks when first painted it will rarely keep that appearance thru<span class='line-break'> </span>a winter. However, I will try again, if you wish it.</p>
<p>I think it was a mistake to try to do anything to the sod<span class='line-break'> </span>last year, as the sod is worn out and then is too much shade<span class='line-break'> </span>The lot really needed resodding and I will see that what<span class='line-break'> </span>Expense you have been at, shall not be thrown away.</p>
<p>Hoping that the matter may be arranged to your satisfaction</p>
<p>I am respectfuly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering</p>
</div>

<p>In regard to exchanging lot #228<span class='line-break'> </span>on Walnut Ave, for one on the stone farm where you<span class='line-break'> </span>have selected your own, I would say that I can not<span class='line-break'> </span>[?] you anything for the curbing, as it would be<span class='line-break'> </span>removed, if taken by the corporation, as was the fence<span class='line-break'> </span>around W<sup>m</sup> [Houghton's?] lot, when I Exchanged with him.</p>
<p>I do not suppose, therefore, from what was said<span class='line-break'> </span>yesterday that you will care to make the Exchange,<span class='line-break'> </span>but if you should, it can be done in this way; you can<span class='line-break'> </span>sell &amp; remove the curbing, or I will remove it for the [stone?],<span class='line-break'> </span>and then I will give you as many feet on the Stone farm<span class='line-break'> </span>as you now own, that is the cost of a 400 ft lot on the<span class='line-break'> </span>Stone Farm being $1080 under perpetual care, you would<span class='line-break'> </span>pay $630 and lot #228 in exchange, this [latter?] lot not being<span class='line-break'> </span>under perpetual care.</p>

<p>Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering</p>

<p>The Grade of your lot can<span class='line-break'> </span>be raised three inches, but not more, as it would<span class='line-break'> </span>not correspond well with the adjoining lots to make<span class='line-break'> </span>it any higher. I think the appearance would be<span class='line-break'> </span>much improved by removing the fence, and placing<span class='line-break'> </span>ornamental granit posts at the corners of the lot &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>at the entrance if you desire; a curbing all around<span class='line-break'> </span>the lot would not look very well, as the lot is<span class='line-break'> </span>somewhat irregular in shape.</p>

The tree in the lot I will remove<span class='line-break'> </span>without Extra charge, if it is cut off, and if [?] the<span class='line-break'> </span>grading; if the stump is to be dug out it will cut $4 or $5<span class='line-break'> </span>more.</p>

<div id="page-1153725">
<h3><a name="page-1153725">CB05_0479</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>479</p>
<p>July 14 [187]7</p>
<p>Mrs E.L. [Eaton?]<span class='line-break'> </span>Commonwealth Hotel Boston</p>
<p>Dear Madam</p>
<p>In looking at your lot today,<span class='line-break'> </span>I find the grade can be raised to advantage some<span class='line-break'> </span>six or eight inches, and if this is done the fence should<span class='line-break'> </span>be taken away.</p>
<p>To take away the fence, put in four new granite<span class='line-break'> </span>corner posts with a number of the lot on one, to cut<span class='line-break'> </span>down the tree in the lot and one outside or both<span class='line-break'> </span>&amp; raise the grade as above, also the myrtle graves now there<span class='line-break'> </span>and to resod will cost $55 and the fence &amp; old posts.<span class='line-break'> </span>I think you spoke of wanting another myrtle grave; [w^d^?]<span class='line-break'> </span>[be?] $7^00^ more if put in.</p>
<p>I would advise that the fence be taken away, as<span class='line-break'> </span>I think the lot would be much improved thereby.</p>
<p>The perpetual care with flowers, if there are no<span class='line-break'> </span>headstones or monuments would cost $350 to $400 and<span class='line-break'> </span>if there are monuments it would be more depending<span class='line-break'> </span>on the value and desirability of the stone. The lot can be [recov-?]<span class='line-break'> </span>[ered?] to the Corporation and no more<span class='line-break'> </span>interments permitted, if you desire</p>
<p>Respectfully</p>
<p>J.W. Lovering</p>

<p>I wish you would make careful inquiries of<span class='line-break'> </span>the men working in your department, and report [?]<span class='line-break'> </span>[can?] when fees have been paid other than [?] for<span class='line-break'> </span>which bills are enclosed, since you havbe had charges<span class='line-break'> </span>of the interments. Providing I get a correct statement<span class='line-break'> </span>of the facts, I shall probably take no further action at<span class='line-break'> </span>this time, but I wish it distinctly understood that<span class='line-break'> </span>hereafter I can retain in the employ of the corporation<span class='line-break'> </span>no person who receives any fee or reward for<span class='line-break'> </span>work done in the Cemetery.</p>

<p>J.W. Lovering Sup.^t^<span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs</p>

<h3><a name="page-1153759">CB05_0514</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>514</p>
<p>Sept 13<sup>th</sup> [187]7</p>
<p>D.N. Skillings Esq.</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Enclosed please find plan<span class='line-break'> </span>of an underground tomb for your lot.</p>
<p>I propose to build the tomb of good hard brick<span class='line-break'> </span>well lain in cement, dimensions according ot plan<span class='line-break'> </span>will slate shelves for the caskets to rest on. The arch<span class='line-break'> </span>of the tomb is strong enough to carry the monument<span class='line-break'> </span>you propose to place there. There is a flight of brick<span class='line-break'> </span>steps from the surface of lot to the tomb. I can<span class='line-break'> </span>build it without the slate shelves, but it will be very<span class='line-break'> </span>much better with them, as when the caskets are placed<span class='line-break'> </span>on each other, they are likely to [crumble?] in. There are<span class='line-break'> </span>twelve shelves, four on each side, and four at the back.</p>
<p>The cost of building this according to plan, of^large^brick laid<span class='line-break'> </span>in cement, with slate shelves, cemented floor, flight of<span class='line-break'> </span>brick steps and slate covers to stairway, moving over your<span class='line-break'> </span>monuments and placing in position will be $800, and<span class='line-break'> </span>if without the slate shelves $675. I would be glad to hear<span class='line-break'> </span>from you soon, as it will take several weeks to get out the<span class='line-break'> </span>shelves if you take them, as I would most certainly advise you to do.</p>
</div>
</div>

<p>Gentlemen</p>
<p>I would call your attention<span class='line-break'> </span>to the fact, that in making repairs on Mt. Auburn St<span class='line-break'> </span>a short time ago, the grade of the sidewalk was raised<span class='line-break'> </span>as much as to cover portions of our iron fence, which<span class='line-break'> </span>will undoubtedly be [met?] seriously injured thereby, if it<span class='line-break'> </span>is not altered before [front?].</p>
<p>When the fence was set, the Town by its Selectmen<span class='line-break'> </span>not only assented to the grade, but did the necessary<span class='line-break'> </span>filling both within &amp; without the fence line, as our<span class='line-break'> </span>vouchers &amp; records will show.</p>
<p>I would request your prompt attention to this<span class='line-break'> </span>matter &amp; hereby notify you that the corporation will<span class='line-break'> </span>hold you responsible for any &amp; all damages arising<span class='line-break'> </span>to them from this charge of grade</p>
<p>Respectfuly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>Sup<sup>t</sup> M<sup>t</sup> Auburn Cemetery.</p>
</div>
</div>

<h3><a name="page-1153781">CB05_0536</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>536</p>
<p>October 30 [187]7</p>
<p>Geo. Henshaw Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>I consider it is very desirable<span class='line-break'> </span>that the tomb on your lot #276 should be removed<span class='line-break'> </span>before it is placed under perpetual care.</p>
<p>Catacombs of brick could be built across the back of the<span class='line-break'> </span>lot, with slate covering stones; each catacomb would be<span class='line-break'> </span>deep enough for two boxes, separated by a slate shelf built<span class='line-break'> </span>into the brick work. To build these catacombs of hard brick<span class='line-break'> </span>well laid in cement, with slate covers &amp; shelves, to box 5<span class='line-break'> </span>of the bodies now in the tomb, which would be necessary<span class='line-break'> </span>before they could be moved, to remove all the bodies to<span class='line-break'> </span>another tomb while the work is going on, and to [reailies?]<span class='line-break'> </span>them, &amp; grade and sode the lot leaving all in good<span class='line-break'> </span>order would cost two hundred and ninety dollars ($290),<span class='line-break'> </span>^the material in the old tomb to belong to us.^</p>
<p>This would leave the centre of the lot clear for a monument<span class='line-break'> </span>and all of the lot in front of the monument would be un<span class='line-break'></span>occupied. The cost of perpetual care then without flowers<span class='line-break'> </span>or monuments would be $300; with a monument it would<span class='line-break'> </span>depend on the value &amp; strength of the structure</p>
<p>Respectfuly J.W. Lovering</p>
</div>

He states that<span class='line-break'> </span>he did not name any price for the repairs to<span class='line-break'> </span>the ivy as he was uncertain what the cost would<span class='line-break'> </span>be until he had completed the work and the<span class='line-break'> </span>order given Sep<sup>t</sup> 18 1877 does not name any cost<span class='line-break'> </span>as it would have had he give stated [figures?]<span class='line-break'> </span>We need the following materials<span class='line-break'> </span>and I consider the charge 2 1/2 loads loam @ $1.00 2.50<span class='line-break'> </span>a perfectly fair and equitable 1/2 " manure " 3- 1.50<span class='line-break'> </span>one 18 sq ft sods " 11.03 54</p>
<p>I trust these figures &amp; 1 3/4 days labor @ 2.00 3.50<span class='line-break'> </span>the explanation will make 28 Ivy plants @ 0.25 7.00<span class='line-break'> </span>the matter satisfactory $15.04</p>
<p>Very Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering Sup<sup>t</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs</p>

<p>I have had the grade stakes<span class='line-break'> </span>set over your lots as proposed when you were here &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>I find that the lay of the land is such that at least<span class='line-break'> </span>300 loads of loam (by actual survey) will be required.</p>
<p>My estimate for raising with loam to the stakes as<span class='line-break'> </span>now set, raising the trees which are small enough to raise,<span class='line-break'> </span>resodding the lots inside of the fence &amp; manuring is $550<span class='line-break'> </span>five hundred &amp; fifty dollars. I will agree that it shall not<span class='line-break'> </span>exceed this sum and I will make it less if I can tho' I<span class='line-break'> </span>do not think it can be well done for less.</p>
<p>Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span></p>

<p>Nov 7<sup>th</sup> [187]7</p>
<p>S.T. Snow Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>I have looked at the Gay tomb as<span class='line-break'> </span>requested and find several large patches of the plastering<span class='line-break'> </span>have fallen. It is too late to replaster this autumn, but<span class='line-break'> </span>it can be done in the spring.</p>
<p>I have never found any of the tombs which were<span class='line-break'> </span>plastered, which could be kept in good order, as the<span class='line-break'> </span>plaster in continualy cracking &amp; sealing off.</p>
<p>Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering.</p>

<p>As to price, I belive the corporation generaly<span class='line-break'> </span>charge less for the same quality of work other<span class='line-break'> </span>any on eelse, this plan being to do the work for<span class='line-break'> </span>the proprietors at as near actual cost as possible.</p>

<p>I send you a corrected bill, which<span class='line-break'> </span>I believe to be a fair one &amp; which I have no doubt<span class='line-break'> </span>will be satisfactory to you.</p>
<p>Your mason set the steps of the lot so high, that it<span class='line-break'> </span>was impossible to make the grade look well without<span class='line-break'> </span>putting in the [ha..?]. As to the sods, that part of the<span class='line-break'> </span>lot which the mason had not [done?] over, was covered<span class='line-break'> </span>with sod so brittle, that it was impossible to save<span class='line-break'> </span>much of it, and it was necessary to strip the sods to<span class='line-break'> </span>get the grade. I have only charged you with what was<span class='line-break'> </span>necessarily used. The charge for watering is taken off &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>the credit for the posts returned put on. The care of the<span class='line-break'> </span>lot should be paid for if the watering is not, as the<span class='line-break'> </span>lot has had as much care as usual, the sod requiring<span class='line-break'> </span>watering &amp; extra care enough to more than make up<span class='line-break'> </span>for the time when the lot was in disorder &amp; nothing<span class='line-break'> </span>done.</p>
<p>Respectfully</p>
<p>J.W. Lovering Supt.</p>

<p>As I stated to<span class='line-break'> </span>you yesterday we cannot go<span class='line-break'> </span>outside of the contract in the matter<span class='line-break'> </span>of lot #2256, and of course no<span class='line-break'> </span>one can be authorized to do so.<span class='line-break'> </span>If you do not wish to pay the<span class='line-break'> </span>bill of $14.00 for myrtle we can<span class='line-break'> </span>remove the myrtle and leave the<span class='line-break'> </span>sod in good order; but if the<span class='line-break'> </span>myrtle is to remain the bill<span class='line-break'> </span>should be paid.</p>
<p>Please advise me at once<span class='line-break'> </span>of your decision so that<span class='line-break'> </span>whatever is to be done may be<span class='line-break'> </span>done at the proper season</p>
<p>Very Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering Sup<sup>t</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs</p>
<p>Nov 16 [187]7</p>
<p>Mrs. F. Almy</p>

The cost of care will<span class='line-break'> </span>be $5.50. The plants &amp; other work that<span class='line-break'> </span>you may wish you will please give<span class='line-break'> </span>us definite instructions about in the<span class='line-break'> </span>spring of 1878. This arrangement will<span class='line-break'> </span>I trust be satisfactory. It is my desire<span class='line-break'> </span>to do all that I can to make it so<span class='line-break'> </span>Very Respectfully J.W. <h3><a name="page-1153813">CB05_0570</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>570</p>
<p>Dec.<sup>r</sup> 17<sup>th</sup> [187]7</p>
<p>Rob<sup>t</sup> O. Fuller Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>The letter which you sent to the Treasurer<span class='line-break'> </span>(Mr Mackintosh) in regard to the charge for repairs on your<span class='line-break'> </span>curbing has been sent to me.</p>
<p>As far as my Experience goes, no curb have been set here,<span class='line-break'> </span>which do not require occasional [?] &amp; repairs. The [man?]<span class='line-break'> </span>who set the curb, is still in our Employ &amp; a most reliable<span class='line-break'> </span>workman, who has, ever since I have known him, done<span class='line-break'> </span>the best job possible, with the stone furnished.</p>
<p>At the time you had your curb set, it was not the<span class='line-break'> </span>custom to put in clamp, which of course adds much<span class='line-break'> </span>to the strength, &amp; which would also have added to the<span class='line-break'> </span>first cost.</p>
<p>Now, inasmuch as the lot has now been clamped &amp; repaired<span class='line-break'> </span>a carefully as possible, I propose to divide the Expense with<span class='line-break'> </span>you reducing the charge from $55 to $27<sup>50</sup> which [?] I<span class='line-break'> </span>trust be satisfactory to you. Please let me hear from you<span class='line-break'> </span>&amp; oblige</p>
<p>Yrs truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>

<p>Dec. 17th 7 [1877]</p>
<p>Dear Miss Hall</p>
<p>I think the best way to<span class='line-break'> </span>make the sod on your lot look well<span class='line-break'> </span>would be to raise the mounds over <span class='line-break'> </span>the graves &amp; resod them, and to<span class='line-break'> </span>enrich the whole lot &amp; put some<span class='line-break'> </span>grass seed over the whole lot. If this<span class='line-break'> </span>should be done early in the spring<span class='line-break'> </span>I think, the whole lot would be much<span class='line-break'> </span>improved. The whole expense would be<span class='line-break'> </span>($8 00) eight dollars</p>
<p>I think it would improve the ap<span class='line-break'></span>pearance of the lot, to have but the<span class='line-break'> </span>for corner posts, and these set a little<span class='line-break'> </span>lower than now. If you think so too,<span class='line-break'> </span>the posts taken out will pay for the <span class='line-break'> </span>change. The levelling of the graves only would<span class='line-break'> </span>cost less.</p>
<p>Yrs very truly</p>
<p>J. W. Lovering</p>

<div class="page-content">
<p>575</p>
<p>Dec. 21<sup>st</sup> [187]7</p>
<p>W<sup>m</sup> G. Thatcher Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>In answer to your favor of yesterday,<span class='line-break'> </span>I would say that the cost of painting the fence around<span class='line-break'> </span>lots #715 &amp; 716 the past season (1877) would have been, for one<span class='line-break'> </span>Coat $4.50, for two coats $7.50. The charge for a bed<span class='line-break'> </span>of myrtle or the grave of an adulte is $7.00.</p>
<p>These charges would be the same during the next season,<span class='line-break'> </span>being considerably reduced from our rates for 1875 &amp; 1878.</p>
<p>As to the care of the lots the price for care <u>without</u> plants<span class='line-break'> </span>of the whole enclosures (#715 &amp; 716) would have been for<span class='line-break'> </span>the past season $6.50 and for plants $5<sup>00</sup> additional for<span class='line-break'> </span>the amount usually put in, tho' more or less could be<span class='line-break'> </span>spent on plants at your pleasure. For top dressing $4.75</p>
<p>For the next season (1878) the care would be $6.25 with<span class='line-break'> </span>plants additional as before say $5<sup>50</sup>, and top dressing $4.50</p>
<p>I should be pleased to do any work which you may<span class='line-break'> </span>desire done the coming season.</p>
<p>It is the purpose of the corporation to do the work at as low<span class='line-break'> </span>rates as possible &amp; it is not done as a source of income in any way.</p>
<p>Yrs truly J.W. Lovering</p>

<h3><a name="page-1153828">CB05_0583</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>583</p>
<p><table class='tabular'><thead><span class='line-break'> </span><tr><th>Original Amt. and Present value of Perpetual Care Funds.</th> <th>Total Expenses for all Care of sode from 1873~1877 on all Perpetual Care lots with G.</th></tr></thead> </table> (B) Perpetual Care of Grass 29,569.50<span class='line-break'> </span>(C) Perpetual Care with G. <u> 121,638.80</u><span class='line-break'> </span>Original Endowments 167,928.30<span class='line-break'> </span>Unexpended Balance <u>24,945.30</u><span class='line-break'> </span>*Value Dec. 31,1877 191,873.60<span class='line-break'> </span>*In 1873 a Reimbursement was made from General Fund of $1708.40</p>
<p><table class='tabular'><thead><span class='line-break'> </span><tr><th>Year</th> <th>Sq. Ft.</th> <th>Amt.</th> <th>Cost for Sq Ft.</th></tr></thead> <tbody> <tr><td>1873</td> <td>59346</td> <td>$2594.59</td> <td>$.044 </td> </tr> <tr><td>1874</td> <td>66876</td> <td>3240.10</td> <td>.049 </td> </tr> <tr><td>1875</td> <td>73829</td> <td>3145.02</td> <td>.042 </td> </tr> <tr><td>1876</td> <td>78750</td> <td>3071.60</td> <td>.039 </td> </tr> <tr><td>1877</td> <td>91951</td> <td>2673.60</td> <td>.029 </td> </tr> </tbody> </table> Average $0.040</p>
<p>From 1844 to 1877, 227 Endowments on P.C. lots with G. were taken $121638.80<span class='line-break'> </span>These contain 91951 sq. feet and marble valued @ $125,122<span class='line-break'> </span>and Granite Monts'. &amp; headstones @ ----------- 24,900</p>
<p>This marble is estimated to last 50 years, or say 42 1/2 years from time taken<span class='line-break'> </span>under perpetual care; as the interest on $1.00 for 42 1/2 years is $7.00 (5% compound) for<span class='line-break'> </span>every $7.00 worth of marble to be replaced, these should be $1.00 at interest (compound).</p>
<p>Taking 1/7 of the value of the marble covered by the contracts for each year<span class='line-break'> </span>from 1844 to 1877, and computing the interest (5% compound) from the time<span class='line-break'> </span>taken, to Dec 31/77 we get the amount by which the original endowments<span class='line-break'> </span>should be increased at this time Dec 31/77 which is -- $9968.21<span class='line-break'> </span>Original endowments <u>121638.80</u><span class='line-break'> </span>Dec. 31, 1877 Estimated value of " $131607.01<span class='line-break'> </span>" " " Actual " " " $142998.39</p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-1153829">
<h3><a name="page-1153829">CB05_0584</a></h3>

<p>J.M. Spelman Esq</p>
<p>Pres<sup>t</sup>. [&amp;c?]</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>The receipts from the New Receiving<span class='line-break'> </span>Tomb which has now been open about a year amount<span class='line-break'> </span>to $471 for fifteen deposits, $100 more having been refunded.</p>
<p>The present fees are $25 for use of the tomb for a [teren?] not<span class='line-break'> </span>Exceeding three months (which is refunded if the body is<span class='line-break'> </span>removed within ten days,) and $4 per month for each month<span class='line-break'> </span>or part of a month in addition. This amount the Mass Hort. Soc.<span class='line-break'> </span>receive on fourth of</p>
<p>In addition the usual fee for interment is charged in<span class='line-break'> </span>advance both for the attendance at the [?]^deposit^, and for<span class='line-break'> </span>removal and interment in a lot in the cemetery, making<span class='line-break'> </span>$10 in case of an adult, and $[3?] in case of a child under ten.<span class='line-break'> </span>The Forest Hills report dated Mch 1876 states the receipts for a year to be $1914 for 76 deposits<span class='line-break'> </span>and the report dated Mch 1877 state the receipts for a year to be $2181 for 76 deposits.<span class='line-break'> </span>The fees there are now $25 for an adult for [four?] months and $5.00 per<span class='line-break'> </span>month for each month [entered?] on, and $15 for a child under ten and<span class='line-break'> </span>$3.00 pr. month for each month entered on. The cost of removal is additional<span class='line-break'> </span>and nothing is refunded. Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering</p>

<div id="page-1153843">
<h3><a name="page-1153843">CB05_0597</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>597</p>
<p>March 29<sup>th</sup> [187]8</p>
<p>S.T. Snow Esq</p>
<p>Chair. Comm. on Lots</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Mrs. George S. Priest intends planting<span class='line-break'> </span>a border of myrtle around her lot between the corner posts,<span class='line-break'> </span>about seventy five linear feet in all which will cost $35 to $40.<span class='line-break'> </span>She has asked what sum will be necessary to place the<span class='line-break'> </span>[myrtle?] under perpetual care, the lot having been sold with<span class='line-break'> </span>the "perpetual care of grass" contract.</p>
<p>The annual Expense for covering, repairing &amp;c would be $5.00</p>
<p>In this connection I desire to call your attention to the<span class='line-break'> </span>fact that in lots under perpetual care in which are myrtle graves<span class='line-break'> </span>kept in order under the perpetual care contract, new graves of myrtle<span class='line-break'> </span>are now often planted for repairing which, no provision is made<span class='line-break'> </span>and in fact it is often a difficult matter to know which it has been<span class='line-break'> </span>agreed to take care of and which not. The myrtle [disptaces?] about<span class='line-break'> </span>ten square feet of sod, and costs probably $1 pr. year. The present<span class='line-break'> </span>cost of a myrtle grave is $7.00</p>
<p>I would like to suggest $17. as the price of a myrtle grave<span class='line-break'> </span>under perpetual care in lots where the grass is already under<span class='line-break'> </span>perpetual care $10 of which amount could be placed in the repair fund.</p>
<p>Respectfuly J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>

<h3><a name="page-1153845">CB05_0599</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>599</p>
<p>Apr. 4<sup>th</sup> [187]8</p>
<p>E.M. Endicott Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Your favor of March 20<sup>th</sup> to our<span class='line-break'> </span>Treasurer (H.B. Mackintosh) has been forwarded to me and<span class='line-break'> </span>I have been to your lot.</p>
<p>The lot, seen at this season, bears Evidence of consid<span class='line-break'></span>Erable care &amp; the grass is now starting up well thru' the<span class='line-break'> </span>top dressing. The lot will be put in order at once, &amp; should<span class='line-break'> </span>your family when next here find anything unsatisfactory<span class='line-break'> </span>I should consider it a favor if they would speak of it at<span class='line-break'> </span>my office, or write me a line, that it may be rectified.</p>
<p>I think if cut flowers have been placed on the lot, they<span class='line-break'> </span>may not have been removed when faded, as many<span class='line-break'> </span>proprietors direct us not to remove them, preferring to<span class='line-break'> </span>do it themselves when ready. There is a wooden trellis<span class='line-break'> </span>on the lot which I think should be removed, as it is broken up.</p>
<p>When here, I think if you would look at the plainting of<span class='line-break'> </span>the fence, and the sodding of the banks in front of the lot,<span class='line-break'> </span>you might think it well to do something to them.</p>
<p>Yrs truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span></p>

<h3><a name="page-1153846">CB05_0602</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>602</p>
<p>April 5 [187]7</p>
<p>Lot #2459<span class='line-break'> </span>Mrs. T.A. Thayer Jamaica Plain</p>
<p>Dear Madam</p>
<p>Part of the trees should be<span class='line-break'> </span>removed which will help the matter of the stained<span class='line-break'> </span>stones. In order to make the lot look<span class='line-break'> </span>well the fence, steps, and surperfluous<span class='line-break'> </span>posts should be removed and the lot<span class='line-break'> </span>resodded and the number cut at a cost<span class='line-break'> </span>of $48.<sup>00</sup> less the value of old iron &amp; stone,<span class='line-break'> </span>say $15.00 leaving [nel?] cost $33.00.</p>
<p>If you can make it convenient to<span class='line-break'> </span>call here again I can explain the proposed<span class='line-break'> </span>improvements better at the lot &amp; I think you<span class='line-break'> </span>will see that what I recommend will benefit<span class='line-break'> </span>the lot very much</p>
<p>Very Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering Sup<sup>t</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs<span class='line-break'> </span></p>

<div class="page-content">
<p>618</p>
<p>May 9<sup>th</sup> [187]8.</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>In regard to the Erection of<span class='line-break'> </span>a headstone on your lot over the<span class='line-break'> </span>[size?] mentioned in the deed as the<span class='line-break'> </span>limit, &amp;.c. two and a half feet,<span class='line-break'> </span>about which some of the ladies of<span class='line-break'> </span>the family made inquiries last<span class='line-break'> </span>week, I would say that permission<span class='line-break'> </span>has never been granted Except<span class='line-break'> </span>in the case of proprietors who have<span class='line-break'> </span>been obliged to Exchange their lots<span class='line-break'> </span>and who therefore had the stones all<span class='line-break'> </span>finished, and I think there is<span class='line-break'> </span>great doubt in looking into matter<span class='line-break'> </span>of permission would be granted in<span class='line-break'> </span>any other case. I have therefore thought<span class='line-break'> </span>it best not to present it at the meeting<span class='line-break'> </span>of the trustees, feeling you would not<span class='line-break'> </span>want it done, with probability of refusal</p>
<p>F.P. Brown Esq.<span class='line-break'> </span>Lot 4449.</p>
<p>Yrs truly J.W. Lovering</p>
<p>May 9<sup>th</sup> [187]8</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>In regard to the asphalt path<span class='line-break'> </span>&amp;c for which you petitioned the<span class='line-break'> </span>Trustees, I would say that the great<span class='line-break'> </span>trouble in the look of the front of<span class='line-break'> </span>your lot is caused by the steepness<span class='line-break'> </span>of the grade. If you are willing to<span class='line-break'> </span>bear the Expense of regrading the<span class='line-break'> </span>borders on front of your lot, I will<span class='line-break'> </span>see that the lots on each side do<span class='line-break'> </span>the same, and will have the path<span class='line-break'> </span>properly gravelled, which will put<span class='line-break'> </span>the whole path in order.</p>
<p>The Expense to you which I speak<span class='line-break'> </span>of will not Exceed $15.00 and if<span class='line-break'> </span>you do not understand the plan,<span class='line-break'> </span>Either myself or the foreman will<span class='line-break'> </span>Explain it to you any week day you<span class='line-break'> </span>find it Convenient to Come up.</p>
<p>F. Whittemore Esq<span class='line-break'> </span>Lot. 2592</p>
<p>Yrs truly J.W. Lovering</p>

<p>Very Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering Sup<sup>t</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs</p>

<p>July 16<sup>th</sup> [187]8.</p>
<p>Messrs Rob &amp; Ross &amp; Sons.</p>
<p>Dear Sirs</p>
<p>I learn through M<sup>r</sup> M<sup>c</sup>Arthur<span class='line-break'> </span>that you desire to begin hauling the manure at<span class='line-break'> </span>once.</p>
<p>I have not intended to have any hauled until<span class='line-break'> </span>after August 1<sup>st</sup>, but if you find it more convenient<span class='line-break'> </span>to do it now, I [?] object so long as you send no bill<span class='line-break'> </span>until Sept 1<sup>t</sup>. There will be no meeting of our Trustees<span class='line-break'> </span>probably in August and no bills will be paid until September</p>
<p>As the quantity wanted was not definitely settled<span class='line-break'> </span>last spring when the price was, I will say now that<span class='line-break'> </span>I shall not want but one hundred cords (100 cords)<span class='line-break'> </span>this autumn.</p>

<p>Messrs Barker [Torrey?] &amp; Co.</p>
<p>Dr Sir</p>
<p>In reply to your favor of the 9<sup>the</sup> inst<span class='line-break'> </span>I would say that when the bill for the foundation in lot<span class='line-break'> </span>#3629 [?]) was [received?], the price was placed at cost<span class='line-break'> </span>owning to the misunderstanding which then [appeared?] to<span class='line-break'> </span>by which I considered was meeting the matter promptly<span class='line-break'> </span>&amp; fairly on our post, and to be all that we shuld do.</p>
<p>Mr. Lennox was here in the early spring and wanted<span class='line-break'> </span>the foundation built in the most thorough way, and it<span class='line-break'> </span>was built of block stone in large blocks in the best manner<span class='line-break'> </span>and this was in my opinion necessary owing to the large<span class='line-break'> </span>amount of clay under this and the aspiring lots which<span class='line-break'> </span>has heretofore given some trouble. When here, Mr. Lennox<span class='line-break'> </span>asked &amp; obtained an estimate higher than the amount<span class='line-break'> </span>charged.</p>
<p>I claim that Mr Lennox did order the foundation and<span class='line-break'> </span>that he is charged less than the estimate given him.</p>

When proprie<span class='line-break'></span>etors order [vanisters?] that we do not keep, but have to<span class='line-break'> </span>send outside for, of course we have to charge accordingly.</p>

<p>734</p>
<p>Dec. 24th. 1887.</p>
<p>H.B. Mackintosh, Treas.</p>
<p>Dear Sir: -</p>
<p>Enclosed I send you two lists of<span class='line-break'> </span>bills for labor and materials which will nearly complete the account for this year</p>
<p>The bills for gardening have all be sent you: the weekly account for Dec.<span class='line-break'> </span>29th. and the monthly Interment account are all the accounts now remaining.</p>
<p>Yours truly</p>
<p>Dec. 24th. 1887.</p>
<p>H.B. Mackintosh, Treas.</p>
<p>Dear Sir: -</p>
